All corporations, limited liability companies and other legal entities which apply for a license must either be organized under the laws of this state, or be authorized to do business in this state, and also be in good standing with the office of the secretary of state. Failure to meet and continue to comply with this requirement, or failure to remain in good standing with the secretary of state, will be grounds for the immediate suspension or revocation of a license. 
(b)  Criminal history. A licensee or designee shall not have been convicted of any felony or misdemeanor, nor shall a licensee or designee have been convicted of any violations of the laws of this state, or of the United States, or any other state, involving the sale of alcoholic beverages, gambling, tax law violations, or the use, sale, possession, manufacturing or distribution of illegal drugs, within seven years prior to the date of the application, nor shall a licensee or designee currently be on parole or probation for a conviction of any such offense. 
(c)  Prior licensing history. A licensee or designee shall not have been denied or had revoked, within the ten years prior to his application, any license to sell alcoholic beverages issued by any governmental entity. No license shall be issued for a location for which the license was revoked within the 12-month period immediately preceding the date of the application. 
(d)  Real parties in interest. A licensee may not be a mere surrogate for a person or persons who would not otherwise qualify for a license. The licensee shall be personally responsible for the management and operation of the business and establishment for which the license is granted. 
(e)  Premises requirements. 
(1)  Ownership of proposed business premises. A licensee shall be the owner of the premises to be licensed or the holder of a written lease thereon for substantially the same period to be covered by the license. 
(2)  Private club or restaurant status for consumption on premises. No license for the sale of alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on the premises shall be issued to any applicant when the location of the facility for which the licensee is being sought does not meet the requirements of a private club or restaurant. 
(3)  Location and safety requirements. Applicant must certify, and provide proof if requested by the county, that the premises to be licensed meets all of the distance and safety regulation requirements for licensed premises under this article, that the proposed location of the licensed premises would not be detrimental to traffic conditions, and that there is sufficient parking area on the proposed premises to be licensed so that it would not be necessary for customers to park in or on the roadways, streets or adjoining property of others. No license shall be granted to any person for the operation of an establishment involving the sale of alcoholic beverages in any area prohibited by law or by county zoning regulations. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, §§ II, III; Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 5; Ord. of 3-24-2011) 
Sec. 4-38. - Wholesale dealers to hold state license and sell on to county licensed retailers. 
Wholesale licenses shall be issued under this article only to those applicants who are licensed by the state to sell and distribute alcoholic beverages at wholesale. Wholesale licensees shall sell and distribute to persons in the county having a valid retail license issued pursuant to this chapter. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § VI) 
Sec. 4-39. - Investigation; fingerprints to be provided. 
(a)  Within seven days from the time the application is filed, the county clerk shall notify the sheriff or such other investigative officer appointed by the county board of commissioners, who shall investigate the character of the applicant and other parties listed on the application and the reputation of the location and make a full report to the board within two weeks of the investigation request, unless additional time is requested by the sheriff or other investigative officer. 
(b)  As a prerequisite to the issuance of the license, the applicant and any potential designee shall furnish a complete set of fingerprints to be forwarded to the state bureau of investigation which shall search the files and forward the fingerprints to the Federal Bureau of Investigation to determine past criminal activity. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § III; Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 6(B)) 
Sec. 4-40. - Notice of application for license. 
(a)  A notice of each application shall be advertised in a newspaper having general circulation in this county and in which sheriff's sales are advertised once a week for two weeks within the four-week period immediately preceding the meeting of the board at which the application is to be considered and acted upon. The notice shall be in such form as the board may prescribe from time to time. The applicant shall pay the cost of such notice in advance to the newspaper to which the notice is delivered for publication. 
(b)  The notice required in this section is only required for new applications, or for applications being made after the applicant's license has been involuntarily terminated or revoked or, when a license expired without being timely renewed. Applicants shall confer with the county clerk or other authorized county official regarding the next available date for the application to be considered by the board after the required notice has been published for two weeks. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § III; Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 4(E)) 
Sec. 4-41. - Written and oral statements and objections. 
(a)  Any county resident or any person owning land in the county may submit a written statement or petition either in support of or opposition to a pending license application regarding the granting of any license under this article. 
(b)  A copy of any objection shall be mailed by the person submitting it to the applicant and the person filing the objection shall certify in writing at the time he files the objection that a copy has been mailed or delivered to the applicant at the address indicated on the application. In the event of a written objection filed in petition form by more than one landowner or resident, only such objector need certify that the copy was mailed or delivered to the applicant as required in this section. 
(c)  Alternatively, any county resident or landowner may make an oral objection to the granting of license under this chapter at any regular or special meeting of the county board of commissioners providing such landowner or resident, or the representative of any group of such objectors, gives the applicant at least 48 hours' written or oral notice of the intent to make such oral objections. The person giving notice, or the representative of any group of residents or landowners giving notice, shall certify at the time of the making of the objection that proper notice to the applicant has been given as required by this section. 
(d)  No objections will be considered unless and until the notice or notices required to be given to the applicant have been given in accordance with this section. 
(e)  Applicants may respond to written or oral objections submitted under this section. It is preferred that such responses are in writing, but the response may be made orally at any regular or special meeting of the county board of commissioners at which the resident or landowner makes or submits the objection. 
(f)  Each person submitting such a statement or objection shall identify the location of his property in relationship to the proposed location referred to in the license application. This may be done by a map, sketch or narrative statement. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § III; 1986 Ga. Laws (Act No. 537), p. 5710) 
Sec. 4-42. - Hearing before board of commissioners; factors considered; determination; rehearing. 
(a)  The application for a license to be issued under this article shall be placed on the agenda for action by the board at the first regular monthly meeting of the board which is scheduled after the date the applicant advises the county clerk that he will have run the second weekly notice as required above. 
(b)  The county board of commissioners shall consider all circumstances that may reflect favorably and unfavorably upon the applicant, the application, and the proposed location. If in the judgment of the board the circumstances are such that granting of the license would not be in the best interest of the general public the board shall deny the application. 
(c)  All objections and statements of support submitted or made by any residents or landowners shall be taken into consideration by the board in determining whether to grant or deny an application filed pursuant to this chapter; however, no such statements or objections shall be controlling or binding upon the board, and the final decision on the application shall always remain within the sole discretion of the board. 
(d)  If a majority of people living within one mile of the proposed location of an establishment oppose the grant of the license and file objections to the grant of the license, a license may be withheld if it reasonably appears that issuance of the license would be a hazard or nuisance to the neighborhood. 
(e)  If an application is denied, applicant may petition the board for reconsideration, providing applicant has additional relevant information to present that was not presented to the board at the time of its original consideration. Such petition must be filed no later than seven days following the date applicant is notified of denial. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § III; Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 4(F)) 
Sec. 4-43. - Form of license. 
All licenses to be issued under this article shall be on forms prescribed by the board from time to time. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 4(H)) 
Sec. 4-44. - Name in which license is issued. 
(a)  A license issued to an individual shall be issued in the name of the individual. A license issued to a partnership, limited liability company, or other similar legally recognized association which is not a corporation shall be issued: 
(1)  In the name of the partnership, limited liability company, or other legally recognized association; and 
(2)  In the case of a partnership, in the name of one of the general partners who shall be the named licensee. 
(b)  A license issued to a corporation shall be issued: 
(1)  In the name of the corporation; and 
(2)  In the name of the majority stockholder or a principal officer of the corporation or the officer or employee of the corporation primarily responsible for the operation of the licensed premises, and such majority stockholder or officer or employee shall be the named licensee. 
(c)  A license issued to a limited liability company shall be issued: 
(1)  In the name of the limited liability company; and 
(2)  In the name of the managing member primarily responsible for the operation of the premises, and such managing member shall be the named licensee. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 4(A)) 
Sec. 4-45. - License term; doing business with expired license prohibited. 
Licenses shall be valid only for the calendar year in which they are issued. No licensee may continue to sell alcoholic beverages authorized under this article after his license has expired unless a new or renewed license has been issued. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 4(G)) 
Sec. 4-46. - Transfer. 
(a)  Application and approval required; exception. A license shall be required for each sales location and shall not be transferable from one location to another or from one person to another, except with the express approval of the board after written application for such transfer and the payment of a transfer fee as prescribed by the board; provided, however, that in the case of the death of a named licensee, such license may be transferred to the administrator, executor or adult heir or heirs of the deceased provided such administrator, executor or heirs, meets all of the qualifications of a licensee as prescribed above, and completes an application form for a license and furnishes a complete set of his fingerprints to the Georgia Bureau of Investigation just as an applicant for a new license. There shall be no transfer fee for the transfer of the license of a deceased licensee to his administrator, executor, or adult heir as provided in this section. 
(b)  Requirements for transfer upon death of licensee. In the case of the death of a licensee, except for good cause shown, or by prior consent of the board, the administrator, executor or heir must comply with the requirements of this section within seven business days after the death of the licensee, or the license of the deceased licensee shall be automatically suspended until such procedure is complied with, and the license shall be surrendered to the board and no alcoholic beverages may be sold at the licensed location until the license is reinstated or a new license is issued. Once the administrator, executor or heir has complied with the requirements under this section, the administrator, executor or heir may continue to operate under the transferred license for the remainder of the calendar year unless the board determines it would otherwise violate this article. If next a transferee under this article desires to renew the license he must follow the same procedure as any other licensee for renewal. If an administrator, executor or heir is not a resident of this county, he may appoint a designee just as any other licensee. Failure of an administrator, executor or heir to apply for a transfer of the license of a deceased licensee within 30 days after the death of a licensee shall result in the license being automatically terminated; anyone desiring a license at the same location after such termination must reapply as for a new license. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § IV; Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 8) 
Sec. 4-47. - Change in business ownership or inability to continue as a licensee. 
(a)  If any licensee withdraws from, sells or otherwise transfers the licensee's interest in the licensed business, or if the licensee is determined to be mentally incompetent by a court of competent jurisdiction, or if the licensee becomes mentally incompetent to the extent he can no longer carry out the responsibilities of a licensee as required under this article, or if the licensee violates this article and is no longer able to fully comply with this article, the licensee or his legal representative shall immediately notify the board and surrender the license. 
(b)  In the case of such a withdrawal, transfer or sale of business interest, or other event requiring a surrender of a license, anyone desiring to have a license at the same location shall, except when a transfer of license is authorized due to the death of a licensee, make an application for a new license in the same manner as for an original license. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 9) 
Sec. 4-48. - Renewal. 
(a)  Application; due date. Except as otherwise provided, all alcoholic beverage licensees with licenses issued under this article shall be required to apply for renewal of their licenses annually on forms prescribed by the county, and must file such application for renewal and comply with all provisions of this article no later than December 1 of the year immediately preceding the year for which the renewal license is being sought. However, no application for renewal shall be considered or approved if the licensee is not in full compliance with this article at the time of the filing of the application for renewal, or at any time prior to the renewal license being issued. 
(b)  Grace period; late fees. Any application for the renewal of a license filed on or after December 1, but prior to 12:00 noon, on the last day on which the office of the county commissioners is officially opened for business in December of that year, shall pay a late fee in the amount provided in the county fee schedule in addition to all other fees imposed by this article. Such late fee must be paid when the late application for renewal is submitted; no late application for renewal shall be accepted or considered until the late fee is paid. 
(c)  Deadline for applying for renewal license. No application for renewal of a license will be accepted or considered if filed after 12:00 noon on the last day on which the office of the county commissioners is officially opened for business in December in any year. Any licensee who desires to renew his license, but fails to file a renewal application prior to the final deadline date in any year, must file an application for a new license in the same manner as an applicant applying for an original license. The board may, but is not required to, notify or remind licensees of the deadlines for filing for a renewal license each year. 
(d)  Approval; referral to board of commissioners. The clerk, or in his absence, the deputy clerk, or other county employee or elected official designated by the board, shall review applications for the renewal of a license, and may approve the renewal applications and issue renewal licenses hereunder on such forms as may be prescribed by the board from time to time, providing the application is in proper form, all fees have been paid, and the licensee is in full compliance with this article. If the clerk or other authorized county official has any reservations about issuing a renewal license, the matter shall be presented to the board for its consideration and action at the board's next regular meeting if one is scheduled prior to the end of the calendar year in which the renewal application is filed; otherwise, the board shall call a special meeting prior to the end of that calendar year to consider the questioned renewal application in order that the renewal application can be acted upon prior to the expiration of the licensee's license for that calendar year. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § III; Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 7) 
Sec. 4-49. - Suspension and revocation. 
(a)  Grounds. Any violation of the provisions of this article shall be grounds for immediate suspension or revocation for cause of the license by the board. Knowingly filing a false application, or providing any false information in any other reports or forms required to be provided to the county or state regarding the licensee's business or sales of alcohol beverages will be grounds for the immediate suspension or revocation of the license by the board. 
(b)  Automatic revocation upon revocation of state license. Upon revocation of a state permit or license to sell alcoholic beverages the county license issued under this chapter shall be automatically revoked and forfeited. 
(c)  Removal of license by authorized law enforcement officers. The board, by resolution, may direct the sheriff of the county and his lawful deputies to remove the license from any place of business of any licensee upon a determination by the sheriff or his deputies that any provision of this chapter or state law pertaining to the sale of alcoholic beverages, has been violated. Upon removal of the license as provided above, it shall be illegal for the licensee to engage in the sale of alcoholic beverages until such time as the license has been reinstated as hereinafter provided. 
(d)  Notice to licensee. Upon removal of a license, the board shall give written notice within three days to the licensee of the reasons for the removal, as well as notice of any suspension or revocation of the license. 
(e)  Right of licensee to request hearing. The licensee may, within ten days from receipt of the notice from the board, make written application to the board for a hearing on the matter of suspension or revocation, including the right of the licensee to present evidence and cross-examine opposing witnesses. Failure of the licensee to request a hearing within the allowed period shall constitute a waiver of any right of further appeal of the board's decision regarding revocation or suspension. 
(f)  Conduct of hearing; determination. If a hearing is requested as provided above, the same will be held within ten days from receipt of the request by the board. The board, after hearing evidence, shall reach its decision and advise the licensee of the same. If the board determines, with or without a hearing, that a license shall be reinstated, the license shall be returned to the licensee on the effective date of the reinstatement as determined by the board. 
(g)  Method of service of notices. All notices required to be made under this section shall be in writing, and shall either be delivered personally or sent by certified mail, return receipt requested, to the other party's last known address, or in the case of notices to the licensee, to the address of the licensed premises if the licensee's address is unknown, or if the licensee can not be located. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 10) 
Sec. 4-50. - Forfeiture of license. 
Any holder of any license issued pursuant to this chapter who, for a period of three consecutive months after his license has been issued, ceases to operate the business and sale of the product or products authorized, shall automatically forfeit his license without the necessity of any further action. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § IX) 
Sec. 4-51. - Display of license. 
Each license issued under this article shall at all times be kept plainly exposed to view upon the licensed premises. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § V; Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 15) 
Sec. 4-52. - Knowledge of licensee and employees of requirements of chapter. 
(a)  Every licensee shall, prior to applying for a license, read and familiarize himself with the provisions of this article, and the licensee's application shall constitute a certification by the applicant that he has done so. 
(b)  Every licensee shall maintain a copy of this article on the licensed premises and shall instruct each employee engaged in the sale or handling of alcoholic beverages on the relevant provisions of this article prior to the employee's selling or handling of any alcoholic beverages. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 17) 
Secs. 4-53—4-77. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - CONSUMPTION ON PREMISES LICENSES 

Sec. 4-78. - Applicability. 
The provisions of this division apply to licenses authorizing consumption on the premises and are in addition to all other general requirements of this article applicable to such licenses except to the extent that general requirements conflict with the specific regulations in this division. 
Sec. 4-79. - Eligibility restricted. 
Consumption on the premises license may be granted only to restaurants and private clubs. Licensees who have a license to sell alcohol by the drink for consumption on the premises may not have a license to sell unopened alcoholic beverages by the bottle or package at the same location; nor may a licensee having a license for the sale of alcohol by the drink or consumption on the premises simultaneously have a wholesale license for the sale or distribution of alcoholic beverages. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 25) 
Sec. 4-80. - Restaurant qualifications. 
To be eligible for a pouring or a consumption-on-the-premises license, a restaurant shall: 
(1)  Be used and held out to the public as a place where meals prepared on the premises are regularly served to the public for adequate pay each day the establishment is open for business; 
(2)  Contain one or more public dining rooms, with adequate and sanitary kitchen facilities and staff to prepare, cook, and serve suitable food for its guests at all times the establishment is opened for business; 
(3)  Have adequate personnel and food supplies available to cook, prepare and serve meals prepared on the premises during any time the establishment is open for business; 
(4)  Have a valid the county health department food service permit and any other applicable local, state, and federal permits and licenses required for food service establishments; 
(5)  Have at least 60 percent of its total sales comprised of the sale of food prepared and consumed on the premises and nonalcoholic beverages consumed on the premises; and, for this purpose, if a restaurant makes a minimum charge, cover charge or admission charge, or any other nonfood or nonalcoholic beverage charge, the amount so charged shall not be counted in computing total sales and shall not be counted as food or beverage sales; 
(6)  Have a permanent seating capacity at tables or booths, not counting bar stools, of at least 25 persons. 
(7)  Be in a facility or building which is safe and in good repair, in compliance with all applicable state, federal and local building codes and fire safety codes and regulations at all times, it is opened for business. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 26) 
Sec. 4-81. - Private club qualifications. 
(a)  To be eligible for a pouring or consumption on the premises licenses, a private club must be a nonprofit association organized under the laws of this state that: 
(1)  Has been in existence at least one year prior to the filing of its application for a license; 
(2)  Has at least 50 regular dues-paying members; 
(3)  Owns, hires, or leases a building or space within a building for the reasonable use of its members, which building or space; 
(4)  Has suitable kitchen and dining room space and equipment; 
(5)  Is staffed with a sufficient number of employees for cooking, preparing, and serving meals for its members and guests; and 
(6)  Has no member, officer, agent, or employee directly or indirectly receiving, in the form of salary or other compensation, any profits from the sale of alcoholic beverages beyond a fixed salary. 
(b)  For purposes of subsection (a)(4) of this section, the term "fixed salary" means the amount of compensation paid any member, officer, agent, or employee of a private club as may be fixed for him by its members at a prior annual meeting or by the governing body out of the general revenue of the club, and does not include any commission or any profits from the sale of alcoholic beverages. For the purposes of this definition, tips, or gratuities which are added to the bill under club regulations shall not be considered profits from the sale of alcoholic beverages. 
(c)  No alcoholic beverage license shall be granted to a private club organized or operated primarily for the selling or serving of alcoholic beverages. 
(d)  Private clubs licensed under this chapter shall be required to maintain the same percentage sale of food and nonalcoholic beverages as compared to alcoholic beverages as is required of restaurants in the preceding section. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 27) 
Sec. 4-82. - Ratio of alcoholic to nonalcoholic sales. 
Should the total sales from food and nonalcoholic beverages reported by any licensee for consumption on the premises not equal or exceed 60 percent of the total sales of all food and beverages for any two consecutive reporting periods, the license may be suspended or revoked by the board subject to the right for a hearing as provided in this article. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 28) 
Sec. 4-83. - Statement of sales. 
In addition to the reporting requirements required elsewhere in this division, the board may require a licensee to furnish a statement from a certified public accountant or a registered public accountant that reports the percentage of the licensee's total sales derived from the sale of food and nonalcoholic beverages sold on the premises compared to sale of all alcoholic beverages sold on the premises in the licensee's most recent reporting period. The failure of a licensee to furnish such a statement within 15 days after being requested to do so shall be grounds for suspending the license of such licensee until the requested statement is received and verified by the board. Any fees charged by the certified public accountant or registered public accountant shall be paid by the licensee. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 29) 
Sec. 4-84. - Records and reports requirements for licenses for consumption on the premises. 
(a)  Sales records; inspection; retention period. All consumption on the premises licensees shall keep and preserve records of all alcoholic beverages delivered to the licensed premises, and purchased and sold by the licensee, and shall keep and preserve records of all receipts for food and nonalcoholic beverages purchased and sold by them. Such records shall at all times during normal business hours be open for inspection by an authorized agent of the county. Such records shall be maintained for a period of at least three years, provided that the board may authorize the disposal of records prior to the expiration of three years if the maintenance of such records is no longer required by the county. 
(b)  Consumption reports. 
(1)  All consumption on the premises licensees shall file with the county clerk, at the time and in the form prescribed by the board, semi-annual on-premises consumption report which shall include, but not be limited to, a signed statement by the licensee of the gross revenues (excluding all nonfood items such as cover charges and tips) for: 
a.  Food and nonalcoholic beverages; and 
b.  Alcoholic beverages, received by the licensee at the licensed premises for the six-month period immediately preceding the report. 
(2)  The report must be filed by July 15 for the first six-month period ending June 30 each year, and by January 15th for the last six-month period of each year. If the board is not satisfied with or questions any report filed, the board may require the licensee to furnish the business records for the period covered by the report. 
(3)  The actual revenues of a licensee furnished in the reports shall be treated as confidential and shall not be made available to the public unless the county must use them as evidence for any legal or disciplinary action involving the licensee for a violation of this division, or unless it is determined that the county is required to release such information under the open records statute or other applicable laws, or unless the county is required to make information available under a court order or other legal process. 
(c)  Other records. All consumption on the premises licensees shall file with the county clerk, at the time and in the form prescribed by the board, any other documents, reports, records, or books of the licensee relating to the licensed premises under the business carried on at that location, as may be required by the board from time to time. 
(d)  Suspension or revocation of license for failure to file reports and other records. Failure of a licensee to file the semi-annual reports or other records as required herein without just cause may result in the suspension or revocation of the licensee's license until licensee complies with such requirements. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 16) 
Secs. 4-85—4-111. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PREMISES AND OPERATION REGULATIONS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 4-112. - Responsibility of named licensee for operation and compliance. 
The named licensee shall be active in the operation of the licensed business and shall be personally present on the licensed premises sufficiently to assure compliance with the provisions of this article. The licensee is responsible for all activities at the licensed premises and for any violations of this article regardless of whether the licensee has actual knowledge of or participates in the activity or violation. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 13) 
Sec. 4-113. - Responsibility of agents for acts of licensed business entities. 
In the case of a partnership, or other legally recognized association, each partner shall be responsible for the actions of the named licensee and the conduct of the licensed business. In the case of a corporation, the corporation shall also be responsible for the actions of the named licensee and the conduct of the licensed business. In the case of a limited liability company, the limited liability company shall also be responsible for the actions of the named licensee and the conduct of the licensed business. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 4(D)) 
Sec. 4-114. - Employees must meet license qualifications. 
Licensee shall not employ in the operation of a licensed establishment any person who can not meet the qualifications for licensure provided in this chapter. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § V) 
Sec. 4-115. - Records to be maintained. 
Each retail licensee shall maintain for a period of 12 months, records of all deliveries of alcoholic beverages made to the licensed establishment by all wholesalers, including copies of the wholesaler's invoices. Licensee shall make such records available for inspection by authorized county personnel upon request. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § V) 
Sec. 4-116. - Products for retail sale must be purchased from licensed county wholesaler. 
No alcoholic beverages shall be possessed, sold or held for retail sale unless purchased from a wholesaler licensed to make sales in the county. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § V) 
Sec. 4-117. - Premises location restrictions. 
(a)  Prohibited proximities. No person knowingly and intentionally may serve, sell, dispense or offer to sell: 
(1)  Any distilled spirits in or within 100 yards of any church building or within 200 yards of any school building, educational building, school grounds, or college campus. 
(2)  Any wine or malt beverages within 100 yards of any school building, school grounds, church or college campus. 
(3)  Any distilled spirits, wine, or malt beverages within 100 yards of an alcoholic treatment center owned and operated by this state or any county or municipal governmental therein. 
(4)  Any alcoholic beverage within 200 yards of any public park or recreational facility of any kind owned by the county either in whole or in part, or by the county board of education, or by any other government or agency or department thereof, except the civic center and golf course, currently owned by the City of Hazlehurst, which are specifically excluded from the terms "public park" and "recreational facility" for purposes of this article. 
(5)  Any alcoholic beverage within a 300-foot radius of a property line of a private residence, except that if the house structure is not within a 600-foot radius of the establishment which is to be licensed, this restriction and prohibition shall not apply and provided, however, that this restriction may be waived if the owners of all of the private residences within the restricted distance consent in writing to granting of a license for the proposed location. 
(6)  Any alcoholic beverage in any building or on any property or grounds owned by the county, except the property commonly known as the "Big House" facility located off the U.S. Highway Number 341 adjoining the lands upon which the Days Inn/Village Inn Motel are currently located, providing such sale or dispensing of alcoholic beverages does not otherwise violate any state law or City of Hazlehurst ordinance. 
(b)  Method of measuring distances. For the purposes of this section, all distances shall be measured by the most direct route of travel on the ground from the property line of the church, school, etc., nearest the proposed establishment, to the side or edge of the building housing the establishment nearest the church, school, etc. 
(c)  Exceptions for new construction. No licensee seeking a renewal shall be barred or prohibited from obtaining a renewal license if a school, church, residence or other facility referred in subsection (a) of this section is constructed or located within the restricted distance after the license has been originally issued, providing that if a licensee fails to renew his license, or allows his license to be revoked or suspended, and he has to reapply for a license, then, in such event, the former licensee shall be subject to all of the requirements of this article, including the distance requirements, just as for an original license. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § VII; Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 12(A)—(D)) 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-21. 
Sec. 4-118. - Interest of landlord in sales of tenant licensee restricted. 
It is unlawful for a licensee to enter into any agreement whereby the rental paid for a licensed premises is based in whole or in part on the volume of sales of alcoholic beverages by the licensed business or whereby the lessor otherwise shares in the profits or receipts from the licensed business's sale of alcoholic beverages. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 14) 
Sec. 4-119. - Days of sales restricted. 
No licensee shall permit the sale of alcoholic beverages on any day or any time when such sales are prohibited by law, during the polling hours of any election being held in the county, on Sunday or on Christmas Day. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § V; Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 19) 
State Law reference— Sale of alcoholic beverages on Sundays, election days, and Christmas Day generally, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-20; local regulation of Sunday sales, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-7; sale of alcoholic beverage to intoxicated person, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-22; furnishing to, possession of, or purchase of alcoholic beverages by persons under 21 years of age, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-23. 
Sec. 4-120. - Stock packaging, storage and handling requirements. 
(a)  Alcoholic beverages shall be delivered to and received at licensed premises only in the original container and only in a conveyance owned and operated by a licensed wholesale dealer (or licensed common carrier acting for a wholesaler). Alcoholic beverages shall be sold at retail only on the premises. 
(b)  A retail licensee shall store alcoholic beverages only on the licensed premises and at no other place. All stock shall be available at all times for inspection by an authorized agent of the county. 
(c)  Any alcoholic beverages found in any retail licensee's stock which were not received from a wholesaler licensed to make deliveries in the county shall be subject to immediate confiscation. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 21(A), (B)) 
Sec. 4-121. - Illumination of premises exterior. 
The exterior of each building in which alcoholic beverages are sold for consumption on the premises shall contain sufficient lighting so that all sides of the building, parking areas, and all entrances thereto are clearly visible at all times. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 21(C)) 
Sec. 4-122. - Cleanliness of premises; inspections. 
All licensed premises shall be kept clean and in proper sanitary condition and in full compliance with all regulations governing the condition of premises used for the storage and sale of food for human consumption. All licensed premises shall be open at all times for inspection by authorized agents of the county. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 22) 
Sec. 4-123. - Consumption in package sales locations prohibited; posting notice required. 
It is unlawful for any person to open or consume any alcoholic beverages on premises licensed for the sale of alcoholic beverages by the package. In each retail package sales location and place of business, where so restricted, there shall be permanently posted and clearly visible to customers, at least two notices in letters at least two inches high, the following language: 

 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 24) 
State Law reference— Breaking of package on premises prohibited, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-26. 
Sec. 4-124. - Sales to underage persons prohibited; employment of underage persons. 
(a)  Prohibited sales. Except as otherwise provided in this section: 
(1)  No persons knowingly, directly, or through another person, shall furnish, cause to be furnished, or permit any person in such person's employ to furnish any alcoholic beverage to any person under 21 years of age; 
(2)  No person under 21 years of age shall purchase, attempt to purchase, or knowingly possess any alcoholic beverage; 
(3)  No person under 21 years of age shall misrepresent such person's age in any manner whatever for the purpose of obtaining illegally any alcoholic beverage; 
(4)  No person knowingly or intentionally shall act as an agent to purchase or acquire any alcoholic beverage for or on behalf of a person under 21 years of age; 
(5)  No person under 21 years of age shall misrepresent his identity or use any false identification for the purpose of purchasing or obtaining any alcoholic beverage. 
(6)  No wholesaler, distributor, or consumption-on-the premises licensee shall allow any person under the age of 18 years to dispense, sell, serve, take orders for, or handle alcoholic beverages. 
(b)  Exclusions. The prohibitions of subsections (a)(1), (2), and (4) of this section shall not apply with respect to the sale, purchase, or possession of alcoholic beverages for consumption: 
(1)  For medical purposes pursuant to a prescription of a physician duly authorized to practice medicine in this state; 
(2)  At a religious ceremony; 
(3)  When the parent or guardian of the person under 21 years of age gives the alcoholic beverage to the person and when in possession is in the home of the parent or guardian and such parent or guardian is present. 
(c)  Effect of proper identification. The prohibition contained in subsection (a)(1) of this section shall not apply with respect to sale of alcoholic beverages by a person when such person has been furnished with proper identification showing that the person to whom the alcoholic beverage is sold to is 21 years of age or older, providing that the person making the sale does not have actual knowledge that the purchaser is under 21 years of age. For purposes of this subsection, the term "proper identification" means any document issued by a governmental agency containing a description of the person, such person's photograph, or both, and giving such person's date of birth and included, without being limited to, a passport, military identification, driver's license, or an identification card authorized under sections 40-5-100 through 40-5-104 of the Official Code of Georgia Annotated (O.C.G.A. §§ 40-5-100 through 40-5-104). The term "proper identification" does not include a birth certificate or school I.D. 
(d)  Verification of age; request for property identification. In any case where a reasonable or prudent person could reasonably be in doubt as to whether or not the person to whom an alcoholic beverage is to be sold or otherwise furnished is actually 21 years of age or older, it shall be the duty of the person selling or otherwise furnishing such alcoholic beverage to request to see and be furnished with proper identification as provided in subsection of this section in order to verify the age of such person; and the failure to make such request and verification in any case where the person to whom the alcoholic beverage is sold or otherwise furnished is less than 21 years of age may be considered by the trier of fact in determining whether the person selling or otherwise furnishing such alcoholic beverage did so knowingly. 
(e)  Section does not prohibit employment of person under 21. This section shall not prohibit employment of a person under 21 years of age in licensed premises if such employment is otherwise not unlawful or the employment of persons under 21 on licensed premises where such persons do not dispense, sell, serve, take orders for, or handle alcoholic beverages. In addition, this section shall not prohibit persons 16 years of age or older from selling or handling packaged or unopened alcoholic beverages for consumption off the premises in grocery stores, convenience stores, or similar establishments. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § V; Ord. of 2-18-2003, §§ 18, 23) 
State Law reference— Furnishing alcoholic beverages to, and purchase of alcoholic beverages by, persons under 21 years of age prohibited, possession of alcoholic beverages by persons under 21 years of age prohibited, proper identification, procedure where false identification tendered, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-23; unlawful sale of alcoholic beverages to, and unlawful purchase and possession of alcoholic beverages by, any person under 21 years of age, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-23.1; persons under 18 years of age not to be allowed or required to serve, sell, or take orders for alcoholic beverages, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-24. 
Sec. 4-125. - Sales to intoxicated persons. 
No licensee shall permit the sale of alcoholic beverages to any person who is in a state of noticeable intoxication or allow persons who are noticeably intoxicated to congregate on licensed premises. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § V; Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 20(A)) 
State Law reference— Furnishing alcoholic beverages to intoxicated persons, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-22. 
Sec. 4-126. - Certain sales and service prohibited in public places; exception. 
(a)  It is unlawful to furnish or dispense alcoholic beverages through kegs, barrels, cylinders or other portable receptacles containing tap or pump-type devices, in which the flow of contents is controlled by the operator, in a public street or in any public or semipublic parking facility or in the common area of an apartment, condominium or multifamily residential building. 
(b)  It is further unlawful to furnish or dispense alcoholic beverages using vehicles containing tap or pump-type devices. The term "semipublic parking facility" includes any privately owned area wherein motor vehicles may be parked by the public in conjunction with any business, enterprise, commercial establishment, office building or multiple-family residential facility. When receptacles are found in violation of this section and the person maintaining the receptacle cannot be identified, the receptacle shall be confiscated and held for 30 days by the county sheriff. The receptacle may be claimed by the owner or lessor, but will be disposed of at the end of 30 days if unclaimed. 
(c)  Nothing in this section shall prohibit persons holding licenses pursuant to this article from dispensing through kegs, barrels, cylinders or other such receptacles inside the establishments or premises approved by the board for a pouring license. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 11) 
Sec. 4-127. - Gambling and disorderly conduct on licensed premises prohibited. 
No licensee shall permit any gambling, betting, illegal lottery, or other device for the hazarding of any money or other thing of value on the licensed premises, except that this prohibition shall not apply with respect to a properly licensed bingo game, or any other activities, not prohibited by state or federal laws to be conducted in a facility or business, or at an activity where alcoholic beverages may be sold for consumption on the premises. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 20(B)) 
Secs. 4-128—4-152. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - CONSUMPTION ON THE PREMISES ESTABLISHMENTS 

Sec. 4-153. - Applicability. 
The provisions of this division apply to licenses authorizing consumption on the premises and apply to such licenses in addition to all other general requirements of this article except to the extent that general requirements conflict with the specific regulations in this division. 
Sec. 4-154. - Illumination of premises. 
All restaurants, including all tables, booths, and other areas where customers are served, as well as, all passageways for customers, shall be sufficiently will illuminated so that they may be viewed by those inside the premises. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 30(A)) 
Sec. 4-155. - Sales in rooms not open to the general public prohibited. 
The sale of alcoholic beverages in any back room or side room which is not open to the general public is prohibited, except that this prohibition shall not apply with respect to private parties that have been scheduled in advance, room service to hotel guests in their hotel rooms, provided a properly licensed restaurant is located on the premises and private clubs. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 30(B)) 
Sec. 4-156. - Hours of sale. 
Consumption on the premises licensees shall only engage in the sale and service of alcoholic beverages between the hours of 6:00 a.m. and 12:00 midnight Monday through Saturday on days on which sales are not prohibited by this chapter. No consumption on the premises licensee shall permit the consumption of alcohol by any person in or on the licensed premises on any day or at any time when it would not be lawful for licensee to sell alcoholic beverages for consumption under this chapter. 
(Ord. of 2-3-1981, § V; Ord. of 2-18-2003, §§ 31, 34(3)) 
State Law reference— Sale of alcoholic beverages on Sundays, election days, and Christmas Day generally, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-20; local regulation of Sunday sales, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-7; sale of alcoholic beverage to intoxicated person, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-22; furnishing to, possession of, or purchase of alcoholic beverages by persons under 21 years of age, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-23. 
Sec. 4-157. - Dancing on premises. 
Patron dancing shall be permitted at facilities licensed for consumption on the premises sales only where adequate space exists and all fire and safety regulations are met. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 32) 
Sec. 4-158. - Sales and consumption on premises only; removal of beverages prohibited. 
(a)  No consumption on the premises licensee shall permit the sale, dispensing or serving of any alcoholic beverage to any person except in or on the licensed premises. 
(b)  All alcoholic beverages sold by consumption on the premises licensees shall be consumed only on the licensed premises. It is unlawful for any person to remove from the licensed premises, or for any licensee to permit any person to remove from the licensed premises, any alcoholic beverages sold for consumption on the premises. Each licensee shall be responsible for ensuring that no person removes any alcoholic beverages from the premises in any container. 
(c)  It is unlawful for any person to drink or have in his possession an open container of any alcoholic beverage on any public street, sidewalk, park, or other public place within the county, or upon or within any motor vehicle on the streets, sidewalks, parks, and public places of the county. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, §§ 33, 34(1)) 
State Law reference— Permitting persons to remove alcoholic beverages to other premises for certain purposes prohibited, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-44. 
Sec. 4-159. - Activities promoting increased consumption prohibited. 
Sponsoring, conducting, or allowing contests or promotions that have as their primary purpose the increasing of the consumption of alcoholic beverages on the premises is prohibited. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 34(2)) 
Sec. 4-160. - Employment of persons convicted of certain offenses prohibited. 
No consumption on the premises licensee shall employ any person who has been convicted of a felony or a violation of any law of any jurisdiction relating to the sale of alcoholic beverages, gambling, or the manufacture, sale or distribution of any illegal drugs for the ten-year period immediately preceding the beginning of that person's employment, or who is then currently on parole or probation for the conviction of any such felony or stated offense. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 34(4)) 
Sec. 4-161. - Sexually oriented entertainment. 
(a)  No person shall conduct, stage, arrange, or permit upon premises on which alcoholic beverages are sold or consumed any live performance that constitutes or simulates: 
(1)  Sexual intercourse, masturbation, sodomy, bestiality, oral copulation, flagellation or any sexual acts which are prohibited by law; 
(2)  The touching, caressing, or fondling of the breast, buttocks, anus, or genitals; or 
(3)  The displaying of any portion of the female breast below the top of the areola or the displaying any portion of any person's pubic hair, anus, cleft of the buttocks, vulva or genitals. 
(b)  No person shall conduct, stage, arrange, or permit upon premises on which alcoholic beverages are sold or consumed the use of artificial devices or inanimate objects to perform, simulate, or depict any of the prohibited activities described in subsection (a) of this section. 
(c)  Nothing in this section shall be interpreted to prohibit performances in mainstream performance establishments, museums, or theaters. 
(Ord. of 2-18-2003, § 35) 
State Law reference— Certain nude and sexual conduct, use of devices or objects to perform or simulate such conduct, and showing and displaying of pictures on licensed premises prohibited, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-41. 
Secs. 4-162—4-180. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - LICENSING, SALE AND REGULATION OF MALT BEVERAGES AND WINE 

Sec. 4-181. - Definitions. 
Applicant shall mean any person or entity applying for a license as contemplated and authorized by this resolution. 
Establishment shall mean any physical location for the storage or sale either at retail or wholesale of malt beverages and wines in Jeff Davis County. 
His , her , he , she , it , they , them , and their shall, as the context may require, include any other gender and the singular or the plural, for a proper reading. 
License shall mean the permit granted to Licensee for the operation of an establishment for the sale and/or distribution of malt beverages or wine in Jeff Davis County. 
Licensee means any person engaged in distribution or selling, at retail or wholesale, any malt beverage or wine in Jeff Davis County. 
Licensor shall mean the Board of Commissioners of Jeff Davis County, or other authority having control of the fiscal affairs of the county. 
Malt beverages shall include "beer" and shall mean those beverages defined by O.C.G.A. § 3-l-2(3). 
Person means a natural person, proprietorship, partnership, either general or limited, firm, association or corporation. 
Wines shall include those beverages defined by O.C.G.A. § 3-1-2(24). 
(Ord. of 1-10-2019, § I) 
Sec. 4-182. - Qualifications of applicants and licensees. 
If the applicant is not a resident of Jeff Davis County, he or she must designate a person who is a resident of Jeff Davis County who shall be responsible for any matter relating to the license. 
(Ord. of 1-10-2019, § II) 
Sec. 4-183. - Granting of licenses (both wholesale and retail). 
(a)  No person shall operate an establishment involving the sale of malt beverages or wine in Jeff Davis County without having first complied with the provisions of this article. 
(b)  No license shall be granted to any person for the operation of an establishment involving the sale of malt beverages or wine in any area prohibited by law or by valid zoning ordinance. 
(c)  No license shall be granted to any person, persons, or officers or directors of any corporation, for the operation of an establishment involving the sale of malt beverages or wine who does not meet the qualifications set forth in section 4-182 above. 
(d)  Any person desiring to obtain a license for the operation of an establishment involving the sale of malt beverages or wine in the county shall submit an application in the form to be prescribed by the Licensor and which shall contain the following information, or additional information as the licensor may from time to time require, to wit: 
(1)  Type of license for which applicant is applying. 
(2)  Full name of the applicant, including any aliases or trade names, and, in the case of a partnership, firm, association or corporation, the name of the individual or agent who shall be held responsible for compliance with the provisions of this resolution. In the event the applicant is a partnership or firm, the names and addresses of all members of the partnership or firm shall be furnished; and in the event the applicant is an association or corporation, the names and addresses of its principal officers, directors and all stockholders The complete mailing and location address of the applicant and the address of the establishment for the sale of malt beverages and wine and the complete mailing address of the person who shall be responsible for any matter relating to the license if that person is not the applicant 
(3)  The name and address of the nearest church and the estimated distance from the establishment. 
(4)  The name and address of the nearest school building, educational building, or school grounds and the estimated distance from the establishment. 
(5)  Whether or not the applicant or any person listed under sub-paragraph (2) above has previously been refused a license. If the answer is in the affirmative, state the month and year of such refusal, the jurisdiction revoking the license and the circumstances surrounding such refusal. 
(6)  Has applicant or any person named in sub-paragraph (2) above, having previously obtained a license, had the same revoked? If the answer is in the affirmative, state the month and year of such revocation, the jurisdiction revoking the license and the circumstances surrounding such revocation. 
(7)  Has applicant or any person identified in sub-paragraph (b) above been convicted within the last two years of any criminal activity. 
The truth of the information contained in said application shall be sworn to by the applicant before a person authorized to administer oaths. 
(e)  A licensee shall not have any vested rights in a license and a license shall not be renewable as a matter of right, but must be applied for and approved annually. However, a licensee may apply for a renewal of his license each year prior to the expiration of his then current license either on the same application form as used for a new license, or on an alternate form to be prescribed by licensor. Applications for a renewal license must be submitted to Licensor no later than December 1st of each year. Any licensee who does not submit his application for renewal of his license by such time without just cause will be*required to apply and qualify in all respects as a new applicant A Licensee may not sell or distribute any malt beverages or wine in a new calendar year until his new license is approved. 
(f)  In determining the question of the granting of or refusal to grant the license provided for hereunder, Licensor shall consider, among other things the following: The location of the establishment; traffic conditions; the uses of the surrounding property; the conviction of the applicant or his employees for the violation of any criminal statutes; the question of whether or not applicant holds a license for the sale of alcoholic beverages; and other relevant factors deemed by Licensor to have a reasonable relationship to the desirability of the issuance of license to applicant for the establishment provided for in this article. 
(g)  Applicant shall notify Licensor in writing within five days of any changes in the information furnished in the initial application or renewal application. The applicant shall attach, with his application, cash, certified check, cashier's check, or money order in the amount of the annual license fee, plus any sum required for an initial license, if applicable. 
(h)  Applications for a new license shall not be considered until after notice of the application has been run two times in the newspaper having general circulation in Jeff Davis County in which legal advertisements and notice of sheriffs sales are authorized to run; the first running of the notice must be at least 30 days prior to the application's consideration by licensor. The notice shall be in a form prescribed by Licensor. This provision shall not apply to applications for renewal of a license which are duly submitted by December 1st. 
(i)  Applicant must comply with all state requirements for the issuance of license, including the furnishing of a complete set of fingerprints pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 3-3-2(c) to be forwarded to the Georgia Bureau of Investigation which shall search the files of the Georgia Crime Information Center for any instance of criminal activity during the two years immediately preceding the date of the application The Georgia Bureau of Investigation shall also submit the fingerprints to the Federal Bureau of Investigation under the rules established by the United States Department of Justice for processing and identification of records. The federal record, if any, shall be obtained and returned to the governing authority submitting the fingerprints. 
(j)  Applicants for a new license shall pay to licensor, in addition to all other fees and taxes required herein, an initial administrative fee of $50.00 to defray initial administrative and investigative costs. This fee shall be tendered with the application and shall not be refundable. 
(k)  After the application has been filed the road superintendent for the county shall go to the business where the applicant proposes to sell the malt beverages and wine and shall determine if the business is located within 100 yards of any church building or within 200 yards of any school building, educational building, school grounds or college campus or within 100 yards of an alcoholic treatment center owned and operated by this state or any county or municipal government. The business cannot be located within 100 yards of any housing authority property unless a license was issued to said business prior to July 1, 2000. The road superintendent shall then submit a written report to the board of commissioners stating his findings. 
(l)  The board of commissioners must review the application and vote to issue the application or deny to issue it after collecting all information required by law and after the notice of the application has been published in the local legal organ A denial of an application shall be delivered to the applicant in writing by first class mail to the address shown on the application. 
(m)  If an application is denied, applicant may petition the licensor for reconsideration, providing applicant has additional relevant information to present which was not presented to licensor at the time of its original consideration. Such petition must be filed with licensor no later than seven days following the date applicant is notified of such denial. 
(Ord. of 1-10-2019, § III) 
Sec. 4-184. - Annual license; fees; term; transferability. 
(a)  An annual license fee for the license provided in this article is hereby imposed and shall be as follows: 
(1)  Wholesale license ..... $100.00 
(2)  Beer license ..... $1,000.00 
(3)  Retail wine license ..... $250.00 
(4)  Combined retail malt beverage/beer and wine license ..... $1,250.00 
Such licenses shall be valid only for the calendar year in which they are issued, and shall automatically expire on December 31st each year regardless of the date of issue. The prescribed fee shall be tendered with the filing of the application required by this resolution. If the license is not granted, the annual fee shall be returned. Such license fees shall be reduced by 50 percent if the license is granted after June 30th of any year. 
(b)  Licenses shall not be transferable from one person to another and shall not be transferable from one location to another without the express written approval of licensor. 
(Ord. of 1-10-2019, § IV) 
Sec. 4-185. - Regulations relating to operation and sales. 
As a condition subsequent to the granting of said license and the possession thereof, compliance with the following regulations shall be mandatory: 
(1)  Licenses granted hereunder shall be prominently displayed in the licensee's establishment, and shall be, together with the establishment, subject to inspection at any time by licensor or any law enforcement agency having jurisdiction of the area of licensee's establishment. 
(2)  The sale of all malt beverages and wines shall be in compliance with the laws of the State of Georgia and the regulations promulgated by the Department of Revenue of the State of Georgia. 
(3)  Each licensee responsible for the payment of excise tax hereunder shall furnish monthly to licensor a report in writing itemizing for the preceding calendar month the exact quantities of malt beverages and/or wines, by size and type of container, for such month sold within the county; such report may be made in the form of duplicate copies of the wholesaler's invoices. Such report shall be delivered to Licensor no later than the tenth day of each month following the month of delivery of said malt beverages and wines. 
(4)  Each retail licensee shall maintain for a period of 12 months records of all deliveries made to said licensee's establishment of malt beverages and wines by all wholesalers, which said records shall include copies of the wholesaler's invoice accompanying said delivery. Licensee shall make available to licensor all such records upon request of the licensor. 
(5)  No licensee shall permit consumption of any malt beverages or wine on the premises of licensee's establishment at any time, unless otherwise approved by licensor. On-premise consumption shall generally be limited to private clubs. 
(6)  No licensee shall sell or make available any beer, malt beverage or wine to minors, habitual drunkards, or intoxicated persons. 
(7)  No beer, malt beverages or wine shall be sold on any Sunday, or Christmas. 
(8)  No beer or wine shall be sold at retail on which county beer or wine (as the case may be) tax has not been paid. 
(9)  No beer or wine shall be possessed or sold or held for sale at retail except beer or wine purchased from a wholesaler licensed to make sales in the county. 
(Ord. of 1-10-2019, § V) 
Sec. 4-186. - Wholesale dealers. 
(a)  Applicants for wholesale license for the sale and distribution of beer, malt beverages and/or wine, shall meet the same qualifications, provide the same information on the application, and be subject to the same regulations as a retail applicant and licensee, except as to residency. 
(b)  Wholesale licenses shall be issued only to those applicants who are licensed by the State of Georgia to sell and distribute malt beverages and wine at wholesale. 
(c)  Wholesale licensees shall sell and distribute to any retail licensees in the county who hold a valid retail license as provided in this article. 
(Ord. of 1-10-2019, § VI) 
Sec. 4-187. - Location of establishments. 
After the application has been filed the road superintendent for the county shall go to the business where the applicant proposes to sell the malt beverages and wine and shall determine if the business is located within 100 yards of any church building or within 200 yards of any school building, educational building, school grounds or college campus or within 100 yards of an alcoholic treatment center owned and operated by this state or any county or municipal government. The business cannot be located within 100 yards of any housing authority property unless a license was issued to said business prior to July 1, 2000. The road superintendent shall then submit a written report to the board of commissioners stating his findings. 
(Ord. of 1-10-2019, § VII) 
Sec. 4-188. - Excise tax. 
In addition to the license fees enumerated elsewhere in this regulation and ordinance, and the excise tax levied directly by the State of Georgia, there is hereby imposed a county excise tax as follows: 
(1)  On beer and malt beverages: Five cents per 12 ounces, or proportionately thereof, so as to prorate the tax on bottles, cans and containers of various sizes pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 3-5-80(2). 
(2)  On wine: Eighty cents per gallon or 22 cents per liter, or proportionately thereof, so as to prorate the tax on bottles and containers of various sizes. 
(3)  The excise taxes, as provided above, shall be imposed upon and paid by the licensed wholesale dealers in malt beverages and wine doing business in Jeff Davis County. 
Such taxes shall be paid to licensor by such dealer on or before the tenth day of the month following the calendar month in which the beverages and/or wine are sold or disposed of within this county. 
(4)  All retail licensees shall furnish to Licensor monthly copies of all invoices from wholesale dealers of malt beverages and/or wine reflecting the amount of county excise taxes paid to the wholesale dealer. Such copies shall be delivered to licensor no later than the tenth day of the month following the month of delivery to the retail licensee's establishment. 
(Ord. of 1-10-2019, § IX) 
Sec. 4-189. - Revocation, suspension and automatic forfeiture. 
(a)  Licensee shall have no vested right in his license, and any license may be suspended or revoked for good cause at the discretion of the licensor. 
(b)  A license may be suspended or revoked whenever in the judgment of the licensor the suspension or revocation of the license would be in the best interest of the general public. 
(c)  Licensor may suspend a violator's license for up to six months for the first violation in lieu of revocation. Suspension of license is an alternative only for a first violation. 
(d)  "Good cause" for the suspension or revocation of such license shall consist of the conviction or plea of guilty or nolo contendere to the violation of any laws or ordinances regulating such businesses (including this ordinance and resolution), or the violation of regulations made pursuant to authority granted for the purpose of regulating such businesses, or the violation of any state or federal law or any county ordinance, (other than traffic ordinances) or the deliberate making of irregularities, omissions, or untruths in the application for license. 
(e)  Upon information to Licensor that there may be grounds for suspension or revocation, licensor shall serve written notice upon Licensee, either by personal delivery to Licensee or by sending such notice to licensee by registered or certified mail addressed to the address in licensee's application, requiring him to appear before Licensor and show cause why his license should not be suspended or revoked. Such hearing shall not be held sooner than ten days from the giving of such notice, and shall set forth with particularity the date, time and place of the hearing on said matter; such notice shall also state the condition alleged which could, if sustained, result in suspension or revocation of licensee's license. 
(f)  Within ten days of the hearing on such matter, Licensor shall render a decision on the matter, notifying licensee, in writing, of its decision, by first class mail In the event of a suspension or revocation no rebate shall be made on any portion of any licensee fee paid. 
(g)  After revocation of any license granted hereunder, no person formerly holding such license shall operate an establishment for the sale of malt beverages or wines in the county without first obtaining a valid license. 
(h)  The sheriff, upon notice of such suspension or revocation from the Licensor shall take the necessary steps to see that signs are removed and that all malt beverages and wine sales cease. 
(i)  Any holder of any license hereunder who, for a period of three consecutive months after his license has been issued, ceases to operate the business and sale of the product or products authorized, shall automatically forfeit his license without the necessity of any further action. 
(j)  Whenever the State of Georgia shall revoke any permit or license to sell at wholesale or retail any malt beverages, beer or wine, the county license to sell malt beverages, beer or wine shall thereupon be automatically revoked and forfeited. 
(Ord. of 1-10-2019, § IX) 
Sec. 4-190. - Grandfather clause. 
Establishments duly licensed prior to the effective date of this article [January 10, 2019] by licensor (or their predecessors in office) pursuant to an existing resolution regulating the sale of malt beverages and wine, insofar as the renewal of said license (or application by new applicants for existing establishments) is concerned, shall not be subject to the provisions of this article as it relates to location and establishment qualifications. However, all existing licensees and establishments are immediately subject to all other provisions of this article, unless otherwise specifically excluded elsewhere herein. In the event an existing licensee shall have his license revoked, or should the Licensee fail to renew his license before January 1 in any year, then such Licensee and the establishment must fully qualify just as any applicant for a new license. 
No provision of this article shall apply to any current Licensee or currently existing establishment, if the enforcement of such provision upon any such current licensee or existing establishment would be violative of the Constitution or the Laws of the United States or of the State of Georgia. 
(Ord. of 1-10-2019, § X) 
Sec. 4-191. - Copy furnished. 
Licensor will attempt to furnish each licensee and applicant with a copy of this article, but failure by licensor to do so shall in no wise excuse a licensee or applicant from strictly complying with the provisions hereof. 
(Ord. of 1-10-2019, § XI) 
Chapter 6 - ANIMALS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Licensing and registration of animals by local authorities, O.C.G.A. § 31-19-3; livestock running at large, O.C.G.A. § 4-3-1 et seq.; permitting dogs in heat to roam or run free, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-6; disposal of diseased, disabled, or dead animals, O.C.G.A. § 4-5-1 et seq.; dogs generally, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-1; dangerous dog control, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-20 et seq.; animal protection, O.C.G.A. § 4-11-1 et seq.; cruelty to animals, O.C.G.A. § 16-12-4; cruelty to dogs; authorized killing of dogs, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-5; rabies control, O.C.G.A. § 31-19-1; liability of owner or keeper of vicious or dangerous animal for injuries caused by animal, O.C.G.A. § 51-2-6. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 6-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Animal control officer means an individual authorized by the county board of commissioners to enforce the provisions of this chapter. 
Dangerous dog. 
(1)  The term "dangerous dog" means any dog that: 
a.  Causes a substantial puncture of a person's skin by teeth without causing serious injury; provided, however, that a nip, scratch, or abrasion shall not be sufficient to classify a dog as dangerous under this subsection; 
b.  Aggressively attacks in a manner that causes a person to reasonably believe that the dog posed an imminent threat of serious injury to such person or another person although no such injury occurs; provided, however, that the acts of barking, growling, or showing of teeth by a dog shall not be sufficient to classify a dog as dangerous under this subsection; or 
c.  While off the owner's property, kills a pet animal; provided, however, that this subsection shall not apply where the death of such pet animal is caused by a dog that is working or training as a hunting dog, herding dog, or predator control dog. 
(2)  A dog that inflicts an injury upon a person when the dog is being used by a law enforcement officer to carry out the law enforcement officer's official duties shall not be a dangerous or vicious dog within the meaning of this definition. A dog shall not be a dangerous dog or a vicious dog within the meaning of this definition if the injury inflicted by the dog was sustained by a person who, at the time, was committing a willful trespass or other tort or was tormenting, abusing or assaulting the dog or had in the past been observed or reported to have tormented, abused or assaulted the dog or was committing or attempting to commit a crime. 
Owner means any natural person or any legal entity, including, but not limited to, a corporation, partnership, firm, or trust owning, possessing, harboring, keeping, or having custody or control of a dog. In the case of a dog owned by a minor, the term "owner" includes the parents or person in loco parentis with custody of the minor. 
Serious injury means any physical injury that creates a substantial risk of death; results in death, broken or dislocated bones, lacerations requiring multiple sutures, or disfiguring avulsions; requires plastic surgery or admission to a hospital; or results in protracted impairment of health, including transmission of an infection or contagious disease, or impairment of the function of any bodily organ. 
Under control means: 
(1)  Confined by fence, pen, cage, or secure enclosure to the premises of its owner; 
(2)  Secured by a leash, chain or lead of sufficient strength to prevent it from escaping from the premises of the owner; or 
(3)  Located under the immediate physical control of a responsible person, provided, however, that if a dog consistently heeds its owner's verbal commands, it need not be leashed to be deemed under control, so long as it is within sight of its owner and remains responsive to its owner's verbal commands. 
Vicious dog means a dog that inflicts serious injury on a person or causes serious injury to a person resulting from reasonable attempts to escape from the dog's attack. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, §§ 1, 7) 
State Law reference— Similar definitions, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-21. 
Sec. 6-2. - Animal control officer appointed; powers. 
The county board of commissioners shall designate an individual as animal to aid in the administration and enforcement of the provisions of this chapter. The person carrying out the duties of animal control officer shall not be authorized to make arrests unless the person is a law enforcement officer having the powers of arrest. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 2(a)) 
Secs. 6-3—6-22. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - DANGEROUS AND VICIOUS DOGS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 6-23. - Procedure not construed as essential element of crime. 
As applied to the owners of dangerous and vicious dogs, the procedures provided for in this article shall not be an essential element of any crime provided for in this article. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 2(b)(1)) 
Sec. 6-24. - Investigation; emergency impoundment. 
Upon receiving a report of a dog believed to be subject to classification as a dangerous or vicious dog, the animal control officer shall make such investigations as necessary to determine whether such dog is subject to classification as a dangerous or vicious dog. Each animal control officer is authorized to make such investigations and inquiries as may be necessary to identify dangerous and vicious dogs and their owners. A law enforcement officer or animal control officer shall immediately impound a dog if the officer believes the dog poses a threat to the public safety. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 2(a)(1)) 
Sec. 6-25. - Classification of dog as dangerous or vicious; notice to owner; right to hearing. 
When upon investigation an animal control officer classifies a dog as a dangerous dog or a vicious dog, the animal control officer shall notify the dog's owner. The notice to owner shall: 
(1)  Be in writing and mailed within 72 hours of classification by certified mail to the owner's last known address; 
(2)  Include a summary of the animal control officer's findings that formed the basis for the dog's classification as a dangerous or vicious dog; 
(3)  Be dated and shall state that the owner, within 15 days after the date shown on the notice, has a right to request a hearing before the board of county commissioners on the animal control officer's determination that the dog is a dangerous or vicious dog; 
(4)  State that if a hearing is not requested, the animal control officer's determination that the dog is a dangerous dog or a vicious dog will become effective on a date specified in the notice, which shall be after the last day on which the owner has a right to request a hearing; and 
(5)  Include a form to request a hearing before the board of county commissioners and shall provide specific instructions on mailing or delivering such request to the agency. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 2(a)(2), (b)(2), (b)(3)) 
Sec. 6-26. - Hearing before board of county commissioners. 
(a)  Scheduling; notice to owner. The board of county commissioners shall schedule a hearing within 30 days after receiving a request for hearing under this article and shall notify the dog owner in writing by certified mail of the date, time and place of the hearing.
