The notice shall be mailed to the dog owner at least ten days prior to the date of the hearing. 
(b)  Conduct of hearing. At the hearing, the owner of the dog shall be given the opportunity to testify and present evidence and in addition thereto the board of county commissioners shall receive such other evidence and hear such other testimony as the board of county commissioners may find reasonably necessary to make a determination either to sustain, modify or overrule the animal control officer's classification of the dog. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 2(b)(4)) 
Sec. 6-27. - Final determination; notice to owner. 
Within ten days after the date of the hearing, the board of county commissioners shall notify the dog owner in writing by certified mail of its determination on the matter. If such determination is that the dog is a dangerous dog or a vicious dog, the notice shall specify the date upon which that determination is effective. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 2(b)(5)) 
Sec. 6-28. - Destruction of dog that has caused serious injury to human on more than one occasion. 
A dog that is found, after notice and opportunity for hearing as provided for in this article to have caused a serious injury to a human on more than one occasion shall be euthanized; provided, however, that no injury occurring before July 1, 2012, shall count for purposes of this section. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 2(b)(5)) 
Secs. 6-29—6-59. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - REGISTRATION AND LICENSING 

Sec. 6-60. - Registration certificate required; nontransferable; annual renewal. 
(a)  It is unlawful for an owner to have or possess within the county a dangerous or vicious dog without a registered dog certification issued in accordance with the provisions of this section. Certificates of registration shall be nontransferable. 
(b)  Certificates of registration of dangerous dogs or vicious dogs shall be renewed on an annual basis. At the time of renewal, an animal control officer shall verify that the owner is continuing to comply with this article. Failure to renew a certificate of registration within ten days of the renewal date or initial classification date shall constitute a violation. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 3(1), (6)) 
Sec. 6-61. - Minors or persons with certain violations or criminal history may not register. 
(a)  Certificates of registration shall be issued only to a person 18 years of age or older. 
(b)  No certificate of registration shall be issued to any person who has been convicted of two or more violations of this article. 
(c)  No certificate of registration for a vicious dog shall be issued to any person who has been convicted of: 
(1)  A serious violent felony as defined in O.C.G.A. § 17-10-6.1; 
(2)  A felony of dog-fighting as provided in O.C.G.A. § 16-12-37; 
(3)  The felony of aggravated cruelty to animals as provided in O.C.G.A. § 16-12-4; or 
(4)  A felony involving trafficking in controlled substances as provided in O.C.G.A. §§ 16-13-31 and 16-13-31.1, from the time of conviction until two years after completion of his sentence, nor to any person residing with such person. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 3(1)) 
Sec. 6-62. - Limit of one vicious dog per owner and one registration per domicile. 
No person shall be the owner of more than one vicious dog. No more than one certificate of registration shall be issued per domicile. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 3(1)) 
Sec. 6-63. - Annual dog license required. 
In addition to the registration certificate required under this division, all owners of dogs shall be required to obtain an annual dog license per animal and shall pay the license fee set forth in the county fee schedule. 
Secs. 6-64—6-84. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - CONTROL AND SAFETY STANDARDS 

Sec. 6-85. - Minimum requirements for keeping of dangerous or vicious dog. 
(a)  The animal control officer shall not issue a registered dangerous or vicious dog certificate to a qualified owner of such dog unless the owner presents evidence to the animal control officer demonstrating, or the animal control officer otherwise finds sufficient evidence, that: 
(1)  Enclosure. 
a.  The owner has a secure enclosure for the dog meeting all requirements of this article; and 
b.  Maintained an enclosure designed to securely confine the dangerous or vicious dog on the owner's property, indoors, or in a securely locked and enclosed pen, fence or structure suitable to prevent the dog from leaving such property; 
(2)  Posting of warning signs. The posting of all entrances to the premises where the dangerous or vicious dog is located with clearly visible signs warning that there is a dangerous or vicious dog on the property and containing a symbol designed to inform children of the presence of a dangerous or vicious dog; 
(3)  Sterilization and micro-chipping. The dog has been both sterilized and micro-chipped; 
(4)  Liability insurance. The owner has obtained and will maintain a policy of general or specific liability insurance in the amount of at least $50,000.00 issued by an insurer authorized to transact business in this state insuring the owner of the dangerous or vicious dog against liability for any bodily injury or property damage inflicted by the dangerous or vicious dog; and 
(5)  Other requirements. The owner has complied with all other requirements of this article and O.C.G.A. § 4-8-27. 
(b)  An animal control officer is authorized to make whatever inquiry is deemed necessary to ensure compliance with this section. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 3(2), (3), (5)) 
Sec. 6-86. - Proximity to certain public structures prohibited. 
In addition to the requirements otherwise specified, no owner may keep a dangerous or vicious dog within 200 yards of any structure or manmade improvement that is an aquatic center, church, convenience store, day care, grocery store, hospital, humane society, library, nursing home, park, playground, restaurant, school, skilled nursing unit or walking trail, due in part to these areas being frequented by children and senior citizens, and in some cases, having food present. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 3(1)) 
Sec. 6-87. - Duty of owner to notify animal control officer of change in status of dog. 
(a)  Escape, attack or death of dog. The owner of a dangerous or vicious dog shall notify the animal control officer within 24 hours if the dog is on the loose, is unconfined, has attacked a human, or has died. 
(b)  Transfer of ownership of dangerous dog. If a dangerous dog has been sold or donated, the owner shall also provide the animal control officer with the name, address and telephone number of the new owner of the dog. 
(c)  Transfer of ownership of vicious dog. A vicious dog shall not be transferred, sold, or donated to any other person unless it is relinquished to a governmental facility or veterinarian to be euthanized. 
(d)  Move of owner and dog out of city. The owner of a dangerous or vicious dog who moves from one jurisdiction to another within state shall register the dog in the new jurisdiction within ten days of becoming a resident and notify the animal control officer of the jurisdiction from which he moved. 
(e)  Move of owner and dog into city. The owner of a dangerous or vicious dog who moves into the city shall register the dog within 30 days of becoming a resident. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 3(4), (5)) 
Sec. 6-88. - Minimum restraint and confinement specifications; exceptions. 
(a)  Restraint of dangerous dogs outside enclosure. It is unlawful for a dangerous dog to be unattended with minors or the owner of such to permit the dog to be outside a proper enclosure unless the dog is restrained by a substantial chain or leash not longer than six feet, and is under the physical restraint of a responsible person capable of preventing the dog from engaging any other human or animal when necessary, or the dog is contained in a closed and locked cage or crate, or the dog is working or training as a hunting dog, herding dog, or predator control dog, subject to the limitations below. 
(b)  Restraint of vicious dogs outside enclosure. It is unlawful for a vicious dog to be unattended with minors or the owner of such to permit the dog to be outside a proper enclosure unless the dog is contained in a closed and locked cage or crate or is muzzled and is restrained by a substantial chain or leash not longer than six feet, and is under the restraint of a responsible person capable of preventing the dog from engaging any other human or animal when necessary. The muzzle shall be made in a manner that will prevent it from biting any person, but will not cause injury to the dog or interfere with its vision or respiration. 
(c)  Enclosure design requirements. A proper enclosure must keep a dangerous or vicious dog securely confined indoors or in a securely enclosed and locked pen, fence or structure designed to prevent the dog from escaping and suitable to prevent the entry of young children. Any such pen or structure shall have secure sides and a secure top, and, if the dog is enclosed within a fence, all sides of the fence shall be of sufficient height and the bottom of the fence shall be constructed or secured as to prevent the dog's escape. Any such enclosure shall be at least 25 feet from any water or gas meter point to protect the meter reader. Any such enclosure shall also provide protection from the elements for the dog. 
(d)  Training, hunting, herding exemptions. In addition to the requirements otherwise specified by this section and O.C.G.A. § 4-8-29(a)(3), the person training a dog subject to this article must be the owner thereof acting in full compliance with state department of natural resources requirements including, without limitation, the requirement for possession of a valid hunting license. Training, hunting, herding or predator control cannot take place off the property of the dog owner unless the owner of the land on which the activity occurs gives express written consent and acknowledgment of the dog's classification as dangerous or vicious. Dogs subject to the exemption in this subsection are only those that are trained to instantly respond to the verbal commands of the dog's owner including, without limitation, a command to immediately heel or otherwise return to the owner. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 4) 
Secs. 6-89—6-119. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - ENFORCEMENT 

Sec. 6-120. - Confiscation of dog; redemption by owner; euthanasia. 
(a)  A dangerous or vicious dog shall be immediately confiscated by the animal control officer or by a law enforcement officer or by another person authorized by the animal control officer in the case of any violation of this article. A refusal to surrender a dog subject to confiscation shall be a violation of this article. 
(b)  Any dog that has been confiscated shall be returned to its owner upon the owner's compliance with the provisions of this section and upon the payment of reasonable confiscation costs. In the event the owner has not complied with this section within 20 days of the date the dog was confiscated, said dog shall be destroyed in an expeditious and humane manner. 
(c)  Criminal prosecution shall not be stayed due to owner recovery or euthanasia of the dog. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 5) 
Sec. 6-121. - Violations and penalties. 
(a)  Owner of vicious dog. The owner of a vicious dog who violates this section or whose vicious dog is subject to confiscation under this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor of high and aggravated nature. In addition to any confinement that might be imposed for a conviction under this subsection, for the second conviction a fine of not less than $500.00 shall be imposed and for a third or subsequent conviction a fine of not less than $750.00 shall be imposed. 
(b)  Owner of dangerous dog. The owner of a dangerous dog who violates this section or whose dangerous dog is subject to confiscation under this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. In addition to any confinement that might be imposed for a conviction under this subsection, for a second conviction a fine of not less than $250.00 shall be imposed and for a third or subsequent conviction a fine of not less than $400.00 shall be imposed. 
(c)  Repeat offenders. If an owner who has a previous conviction for a violation of this section knowingly and willfully fails to comply with the provisions of this section, such owner shall be guilty of a misdemeanor of high and aggravated nature if the owner's dog attacks or bites a human being under circumstances constituting another violation of this section. The owner of a dog who is convicted for a violation of this subsection shall be punished by a fine of not less than $1,000.00 or by imprisonment for not less than one year or by both such fine and imprisonment. 
(d)  Violations leading to injury to or death of human. An owner who knowingly and willfully fails to comply with this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor of high and aggravated nature if the owner's dog aggressively attacks and causes severe injury or death of a human being under circumstances constituting a violation of this section. The owner of a dog who is convicted for a violation of this subsection shall be punished by a fine of not less than $1,000.00 or by imprisonment for not less than one year or by both fine and imprisonment. In addition to the penalties for violations under this section, the dog involved shall be immediately confiscated by the animal control officer or by a law enforcement officer or another person authorized by the animal control officer and placed in quarantine for the proper length of time as determined by the county board of health, and, thereafter, the dog shall be destroyed in an expeditious and humane manner. 
(e)  Exception for injury to trespassers on owner's property. No owner of a dog shall be held criminally liable under this section for injuries inflicted by said owner's dog to any human being willfully trespassing on the owner's property. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012, § 6) 
Chapter 8 - BUILDINGS AND CONSTRUCTION[1] 
Footnotes:
