Const., art. 9, sec. 2, ¶ 3(12); ordinances relating to repair, closing and demolition of dwellings unfit for human habitation, O.C.G.A. § 36-61-11; authority to demolish structures where drug crimes are committed, O.C.G.A. § 41-2-7; authority to repair, close or demolish unfit buildings or structures, O.C.G.A. § 41-2-7; county or municipal ordinances relating to unfit buildings or structures, O.C.G.A. § 41-2-9; statewide application of minimum standard codes, codes requiring adoption by municipality or county, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-25; enforcement of codes, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-26; providing of fire escapes by building owners, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-50. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 8-1—8-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - CONSTRUCTION CODES 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Secs. 8-19—8-39. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - ELECTRICAL 

Sec. 8-40. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Dwelling and place of business include buildings of any type of construction without limitation, and shall specifically include mobile homes and manufactured housing units. 
Permit issuer means the county official designated by the county board of commissioners to issue the electrical permit as provided in this division. 
Provider of electrical service means any utility company or person, firm, corporation, or partnership which sells, furnishes or delivers for sale electrical service within the county. 
Purchaser means any person, firm, corporation, partnership, society, club, or association of persons acting together as a unit who purchase or cause to be purchased electrical service within the county. 
(Ord. of 9-21-1995, § 1; Ord. of 3-9-2000, § 1) 
Sec. 8-41. - Violations and penalties. 
A violation of this division is a misdemeanor offense punishable by a fine of no more than $200.00. All alleged violations of this division shall be tried in the magistrate court of the county. 
(Ord. of 9-21-1995, § 5) 
Sec. 8-42. - County board of tax assessors personnel designated as permit issuers. 
Staff personnel of the office of the county board of tax assessors are hereby designated as permit issuers in lieu of the clerk to the county board of commissioners. Such designation shall remain effective unless and until the board of commissioners should designate other personnel to perform such function. 
(Ord. of 9-21-1995, § 1; Ord. of 3-9-2000, § 1) 
Sec. 8-43. - Electrical permit required; exceptions. 
(a)  No person or provider of electrical service shall furnish electricity to any new purchaser, reconnect or re-establish electrical service to any existing purchaser, or furnish additional electrical services to any existing purchaser where new electrical services are being added, until the purchaser obtains a valid electrical permit from the permit issuer of the county. Before the occupation of any premises as a dwelling or place of business, and before the issuance of an electrical permit, the permit issuer shall determine that the purchaser has obtained any permit required by the county board of health and any other permit that may be required by any county building regulation. 
(b)  In addition, before the permit issuer can issue an electrical permit to a purchaser who wants electrical service furnished to a mobile home or manufactured housing unit, the purchaser must provide proof to the permit issuer that purchaser has properly registered the mobile home or manufactured housing unit with, and obtained a current year registration decal from, the office of the county tax commissioner. 
(c)  The provisions of this section shall not apply to restoration of service by the provider of electrical service to a purchaser who had previously been disconnected due to nonpayment of utility bills or actions of the elements. In addition, the provisions of this section shall not apply to any service site that existed prior to January 1, 1991. 
(Ord. of 9-21-1995, § 2; Ord. of 3-9-2000, §§ 2—4) 
Sec. 8-44. - Providers to furnish list of electrical service connections. 
(a)  All electrical service providers in the county shall provide to the office of the county tax assessor a copy of the list of service connections that such providers are required to provide to the county health department. The list shall be furnished to the tax assessor's office at the same time and in the same manner as required for the copy provided to the county health department except as otherwise provided in this section. 
(b)  In addition to the information furnished to the county health department, the electrical service provider shall include in the required list a statement as to whether the electrical service was provided to a mobile home or manufactured housing unit, if such information is available to the electrical service provider. 
(Ord. of 9-21-1995, § 7; Ord. of 3-9-2000, § 3) 
ARTICLE III. - MANUFACTURED HOMES, TRAILERS, MOBILE HOMES, AND MOBILE HOME PARKS 

Sec. 8-50. - Definitions. 
Mobile homes, manufactured home, or trailer. These terms are to be considered synonymous and to refer to: 
Any structure designed or used for residential occupancy or other use built upon or having a frame(s) or chassis to which wheels may be attached by which it may move or be moved upon a highway, whether or not such structure actually has, at any given time, such wheels attached, including any such vehicle which has been placed on a masonry or other stationary foundation. This definition shall not include travel trailers of recreational vehicles when such vehicles are not used for permanent or semi-permanent living or sleeping quarters. 
Mobile home park. Any lot, tract, or parcel of land used, maintained or intended to be used, leased or rented for occupancy by two or more mobile homes together with accessory structures provided in connection therewith. This definition shall not include mobile home sales lots on which unoccupied mobile homes are parked for the purpose of inspection and sale nor shall it include property containing two or more mobile homes occupied by family members of the land owner. 
Mobile home, manufactured home, trailer subdivision. All divisions of a tract or parcel whether immediate or future, for sale, legacy or other development, whether partially or in whole, for the accommodation of mobile homes, manufactured homes, and which result in separate ownership by more than one person of the subdivided tract or parcels. 
Location Permits. A location permit must be obtained by any individual or business seeking to locate a home within the county as provided by this article, unless otherwise exempted. All manufactured homes over ten years old shall be subject to an inspection prior to the issuance of a location permit unless otherwise exempt. 
Inspection official. A person designated by the county board of commissioners to inspect manufactured homes, mobile homes, and trailers. 
(Ord. of 12-19-2016) 
Sec. 8-51. - Moving or relocating a manufactured home, mobile home or trailer from one location in the county to another. 
(a)  Anyone desiring to move or relocate a manufactured home, mobile home or trailer must first submit an application requesting the same to the county board of commissioners' office. 
(b)  At the time an application for relocation is submitted, the inspection official shall inspect the manufactured home to determine if the home is suitable for relocation and that the home complies with the minimum health and safety standards set forth; 
(c)  Once the inspecting official has inspected the manufactured home he or she shall submit his or her recommendation for the approval or denial for a permit for relocation to the county board of commissioners who shall then vote on the application for the permit. 
(d)  No location permit to move or relocate a manufactured home shall be issued unless the following criteria have been met: 
(1)  The applicant provides proof that all outstanding property taxes are paid in full at the time of said application; 
(2)  The applicant provides a copy of the sewage and septic permit issued by the health inspector; 
(3)  The applicant provides the name, contact information, proof of liability insurance and bond of the company that is responsible for relocation the manufactured home; 
(4)  The designated inspecting official has determined that the home is intact and structurally sound and capable of being moved to a different location without being severally damaged or destroyed during the move and that the home complies with the minimum health and safety standards set forth herein; 
(5)  The county board of commissioners has voted to approve the issuance of the permit. 
Failure to meet any of the requirements of this section shall result in denial of an application for location of a manufactured home. 
(Ord. of 12-19-2016) 
Sec. 8-52. - Permits—Moving/relocating within the county. 
The cost of a permit required for moving or relocating a manufactured home, mobile home or trailer in the county shall be $25.00. 
All permits issued under the terms of this division shall indicate the date issued. Any permits issued hereunder shall be valid only for the specified manufactured home and for the location of such manufactured home as indicated on the permit. 
Nothing contained in this section shall be so construed as to relieve any person from the responsibility of obtaining a relocation permit each time such person moves or relocates a manufactured home. 
Permits shall be valid for 60 days. 
Moving or relocating a manufactured home in violation of this section shall subject an owner, a retailer, and/or a manufactured home transporter to a fine not to exceed $1,000.00. 
(Ord. of 12-19-2016) 
Sec. 8-53. - Moving or relocating a manufactured home, mobile home or trailer from outside of Jeff Davis County to a location within the county. 
(a)  Anyone desiring to move or relocate a manufactured home, mobile home or trailer from outside Jeff Davis County to within the county must first submit an application requesting the same to the county board of commissioners' office. 
(b)  At the time that an application for relocation is sought, no manufactured home that is ten years old or older, as determined by its manufactured date, shall be allowed to relocate within the county and no permit for the same shall be issued if said manufactured home unless the home passes inspection by the inspection official and that the home is deemed habitable by the local health department standards. 
(c)  After an application for relocation is completed, the manufactured home at issue must be inspected by the designated county inspecting official to determine if the manufactured home is suitable for relocation and that the home complies with the minimum health and safety standards set forth herein; 
(d)  Once the inspecting official has inspected the manufactured home he or she shall submit his or her recommendation for the approval or denial for a permit to the county board of commissioners who shall then vote on the application for the permit. 
(e)  No location permit to move or relocate a manufactured home shall be issued unless the following criteria have been met: 
(1)  The applicant provides proof that all outstanding property taxes are paid in full at the time of said application; 
(2)  The applicant provides a copy of the sewage and septic permit issued by the health inspector; 
(3)  The applicant provides the name, contact information, proof of liability insurance and bond of the company that is responsible for relocation of the manufactured home; 
(4)  The designated inspecting official has determined that the home is intact and structurally sound and capable of being moved to a different location without being severally damaged or destroyed during the move and that the home complies with the minimum health and safety standards set forth herein; 
(5)  The county board of commissioners has voted to approve the issuance of the permit. 
Failure to meet any of the requirements of this section shall result in denial of an application for location of a manufactured home. 
(Ord. of 12-19-2016) 
Sec. 8-54. - Permits—Moving/relocating from outside the county to within the county. 
The cost of a permit required for moving or relocating a manufactured home, mobile home or trailer into the county shall be $40.00. 
All permits issued under the terms of this division shall indicate the date issued. Any permits issued hereunder shall be valid only for the specified manufactured home and for the location of such manufactured home as indicated on the permit. 
Nothing contained in this section shall be so construed as to relieve any person from the responsibility of obtaining a relocation permit each time such person moves or relocates a manufactured home. 
Permits shall be valid for 60 days. 
Moving or relocating a manufactured home in violation of this section shall subject an owner, a retailer, and/or a manufactured home transporter to a fine not to exceed $1,000.00. 
(Ord. of 12-19-2016) 
Sec. 8-55. - Abandoned manufactured homes. 
(a)  Any manufactured home abandoned by its owner or any manufactured home transporter on private property or public right-of-way in the county shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and subject to a fine not to exceed $1,000.00 and up to 60 days in jail. 
(b)  Both the owner and the transporter may be charged with the offense described herein. 
(c)  A manufactured home shall be considered abandoned if it is left on a public right-of-way for a period of five days and is not otherwise removed from said right-of-way during that time or if it is left on private property for a period of 180 consecutive days unless the county board of assessors is notified by the owner that the property will be vacant for a period of time. 
(d)  If a manufactured home is so abandoned, the county may take all reasonable steps to remove the manufactured home from the private property or right-of-way. The cost associating with said removal shall be chargeable to both the owner and the transporter. In such event, if the sale of the manufactured home is necessary to recover said costs, the county may take all legal avenues available to dispose of said manufactured home, including issuing a fi fa for said cost and selling the manufactured home in the same manner that a manufactured home would be sold to recover for any outstanding ad valorem tax. 
(Ord. of 12-19-2016) 
Sec. 8-56. - Mobile home park. 
Any one desiring to set up a mobile home park in the county must first submit an application for a permit to the county board of commissioners along with a $50.00 application fee. 
Once the application has been submitted the inspection official shall then inspect all of the mobile homes that are to be located in the mobile home park. 
Once the inspecting official has inspected the manufactured home he or she shall submit his or her recommendation for the approval or denial for a permit to the county board of commissioners who shall then vote on the application for the permit. 
If the application is approved the mobile home park owner shall then pay to the county the sum of $100.00 for a mobile home park permit. The permit shall expire at the end of three years. At the expiration of the permit the mobile home park owner must apply for a new permit. If at any time during the term of a permit, the mobile home park owner desires to add an additional mobile home or homes into the park then he or she must comply with the application process as set forth herein for relocating mobile homes into the county. 
All mobile home parks shall be classified as commercial property and the owner of said mobile home park shall be taxed per hook up. 
All mobile homes located in a mobile home park shall be subject to all of the provisions set forth in this article. 
Failure of a mobile home park owner to comply with any of the provisions set forth in this article shall result in a fine of $1,000.00 and up to 60 days in jail and shall be required to remove the homes that are in non-compliance from the county at his or her expense. 
(Ord. of 12-19-2016) 
Sec. 8-57. - Minimum health and safety standards. 
Every pre-owned manufactured home shall be in compliance with the Federal Manufactured Housing Construction and Safety Standards Act 42 U.S.C. 5401-5445 (the HUD Code) and shall not have been altered in such a way that the home no longer meets the HUD requirements. 
All floors, interior walls and ceiling shall be in sound condition. Doors and windows shall be operable, watertight and in good working condition. 
The exterior of all manufactured homes shall be free of loose or rotting boards and any other condition that may allow rain or moisture to invade the interior of the home. The roof shall be intact and contain no obvious defects that would allow water to seep into the home. 
Every plumbing fixture, water and waste pipe of all manufactured homes shall be in a sanitary working condition when properly connected and shall be free from leaks and obstructions. Each home shall contain a kitchen sink, a bathroom, a tub or shower, a toilet and running water. 
Electrical systems shall be properly installed and shall be in working condition. Distribution panels shall be in compliance with the approved listing, complete with required breakers with all unused openings covered with solid covers approved and listed for that purpose. Each home shall contain a working hot water heater. 
Each bedroom of a manufacture home shall have at least one operating window of sufficient size to allow egress if necessary. 
The kitchen shall have at least one operating window or other ventilation device. 
Each manufactured home shall contain one operable battery powered smoke detector in each bedroom and in the kitchen, which must be installed in accordance with the manufacturer's recommendations. 
(Ord. of 12-19-2016) 
Sec. 8-58. - Miscellaneous. 
All mobile homes brought into the county shall be set up and anchored. 
All mobile homes brought into the county shall have skirting installed no later than 45 days after the mobile home has been set up. 
(Ord. of 12-19-2016) 
Chapter 10 - BUSINESSES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Commerce and trade generally, O.C.G.A. § 10-1-1 et seq.; professions and businesses generally, O.C.G.A. § 43-1-1 et seq.; county authority to impose business regulatory fees, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-8(a); exclusion of certain veterans and blind persons from county regulatory fees, O.C.G.A. § 43-12-1; authority for imposition of punishment for failure to comply with regulatory fee ordinances, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-8; county authority to levy occupational taxes, O.C.G.A. §§ 48-13-6(a), 48-13-7; imposition of regulatory fees by local governments on certain businesses, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-8 et seq.; issuance of local business licenses, O.C.G.A. § 36-60-6; investigation of business for issuance of county or municipal license, O.C.G.A. § 36-60-9. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 10-1—10-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - TIMBER OPERATIONS 

Sec. 10-19. - Purpose and intent. 
This article is intended to require notice of timber harvesting operations within the unincorporated areas of the county pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 12-6-24, and, in accordance with state statute title 32, highways, bridges and ferries, O.C.G.A. § 32-1-1 et seq., to provide regulations further governing use of public roads by persons engaged in the timber harvesting operations in order to assure the public safety and to protect the county roadways and environment. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 10-20. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Notice means a notice required to be given to the county public works department by the timber harvester as provided herein. 
Surety bond means a valid surety bond, executed by a surety corporation authorized to transact business in this state, protecting the county against any damage caused by such person or firm in an amount specified by the county board of commissioners not exceeding $5,000.00 or, at the option of the timber harvester, a valid irrevocable letter of credit issued by a bank or savings and loan association, as defined in O.C.G.A. § 7-1-4 in the amount of an in lieu of such bond. Any such surety bond or letter of credit shall be in form prescribed by or acceptable to the county administrator and shall be for the calendar year in which delivered. 
Timber means softwood or hardwood trees harvested for commercial purposes. 
Timber harvester means any person harvesting standing timber in any unincorporated area of the county for delivery as pulpwood, logs, poles, posts, or wood chips to any wood yard or processing plant located inside or outside this state. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 10-21. - Enforcement, violations and penalties. 
(a)  Notice of violation. Upon notice from the issuing authority, work on any project that is being done contrary to the provisions of this article shall be immediately stopped. Such notice shall be in writing and shall be given to the timber harvester and the owner of the subject property, and shall state the conditions under which work may resume. When an emergency exists, written notice shall not be required. If the conditions are not brought into compliance within five business days of the notice, the county road department shall be authorized to accomplish the work with costs thereof to be reimbursed by the timber harvester, and any violation of the provisions of this article shall be punished as for a misdemeanor. 
(b)  Prosecution and penalties. Any person violating any of the provisions of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor prosecutable in the county magistrate court and punishable by a fine not to exceed $500.00 and imprisonment in the county jail for a period of not longer than 12 months. 
(c)  Liability for damages. The imposition of any fine or other sentence pursuant to this section shall in no way limit the liability of any person for damage done to public property or public rights-of-way, and the county shall be authorized to additionally pursue recovery for any such damage by any and all means permitted by law or in equity, to include, without limitation, the filing of a suit for damages, or the seeking of injunctive relief to stop any such damage. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 10-22. - Notices of to be provided to county road department. 
(a)  Notice of intent to harvest. Prior written notice shall be required of any timber harvester harvesting timber in the unincorporated areas of the county for each separate tract to be harvested. The written notice shall be delivered to the county road department in such form and containing such information as set forth in O.C.G.A. § 12-6-24(b)(1). Notice shall be effective only as to the tract described therein upon receipt by the county road department as confirmed by written acknowledgment from the county road department to the timber harvester and compliance with all other applicable requirements of this article. 
(b)  Notice of completion of harvest. The timber harvester shall give written notification to the county road department supervisor upon completion of the timber harvesting operations. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
State Law reference— Authority of county to require notice, O.C.G.A. § 12-6-24. 
Sec. 10-23. - Notices of to be provided to county board of tax assessors. 
(a)  Notice of intent to harvest. Prior to initiating any timber harvesting activities in the county, the timber harvesting contractor shall give written notification to the county board of assessors within 24 hours prior to commencing start-up activities, moving in of equipment or cutting of any trees. The notice shall be in the form designated by the board of county commissioners, a copy of which is available in the office of the county clerk. 
(b)  Notice of completion of harvest. Upon completion of the harvesting of the timber identified in the notice of intent to harvest, the timber harvesting contractor shall give oral notification in person or by telephone to the tax assessor's office that the harvesting activities have been completed. 
(c)  Prosecution and penalties for failure to report. The penalty for failure to comply with the reporting requirements set out in this section shall be a fine not to exceed $1,000.00 or 12 months imprisonment in the county jail. Citations for violation of this section shall be prosecuted in the county magistrate court. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
State Law reference— Assessment of standing timber for ad valorem taxation, O.C.G.A. § 48-5-7.5. 
Sec. 10-24. - Surety bond. 
(a)  When required. A surety bond shall not be required prior to the effective date of the notice of intent to harvest. However, following the giving of any notice, in the event that the county road department superintendent determines that any activities relating to the timber harvesting are being conducted in a manner that poses likelihood of damage to any public rights-of-way or danger to the public safety, the county road department shall be authorized to demand a surety bond from the timber harvester. 
(b)  Contest of bond requirement; administrative hearing. The surety bond shall be delivered to the county road department within three business days following receipt of written demand for the same, unless within the time a written notice of appeal is received by the county road department contesting the requirement of the surety bond. In the event of such contest, the county road department shall, no later than five business days, schedule an administrative hearing in such matter before the county administrator, who shall deliver a decision within three business days of the hearing. The decision of the county administrator shall be conclusive and binding for all purposes. 
(c)  Suspension of harvesting during contest proceeding. Following any contest as provided in subsection (b) of this section, all timber harvesting authorized pursuant to the applicable notice of intent to harvest shall be suspended until the surety bond, if any, is delivered to the county road department as required by the county administrator. 
(d)  Amount and character of bond. The amount of the bond shall not exceed $5,000.00. The bond shall indemnify the county against any and all damage caused, as a result of the timber harvesting and related activities, to any county roads, rights-of-way, points of egress or other public property. The surety bond shall also indemnify the county for any costs incurred in the cleanup of waste or debris left on public property as a result of the timber harvesting. 
(e)  Release of bond. Upon completion of any necessary repairs to public property and removal of all waste and debris, the county will release the timber harvester from the surety bond. 
(f)  Bond does not limit liability for damages. In no event shall the delivery of a surety bond limit the liability of any person engaged in timber harvesting and related activities for damages to public property or rights-of-way or for other personal injury or property damage. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
State Law reference— Authority of county to require bond, O.C.G.A. § 12-6-24. 
Sec. 10-25. - Culverts. 
Prior to commencing timber harvesting operations, the county road department superintendent shall inspect the point of access to the public road from the tract described in the notice in order to determine its suitability. If a culvert is required at the point of access, it shall be promptly installed by the timber harvester as directed by the county road department superintendent. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 10-26. - Warning signs. 
Prior to commencing any timber harvesting operations, the timber harvester shall post two signs in each direction from the point of access onto the involved public road. One sign at a distance of 1,000 feet from the point of access stating: "Warning: logging operations ahead" and one sign at a distance of 500 feet stating: "Slow truck entering highway." All signs shall be 36 inches by 36 inches, erected in a diamond shape, painted orange with black legend and posted at least three feet from the travel surface of the roadway. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 10-27. - Roadway safety. 
During the period of operations, the timber harvester shall comply with the following: 
(1)  Operations on public ways prohibited. All harvesting operations shall be conducted on the tract identified in the notice and off public roads and rights-of-way. Logging and skidding of logs on public roads and rights-of-way are strictly prohibited. 
(2)  Ditches to be kept free of debris. Ditches constituting a part of the public drainage system or otherwise benefitting a public right-of-way shall be kept clear of all debris and residue at all times to permit proper drainage. 
(3)  Road and right-of-way obstruction prohibited. There shall be no blockage of public roads or rights-of-way at the access site, and all public roads and rights-of-way must remain open and kept free of debris and residue at all times. No equipment, trucks, trailers, or other personal property shall be parked or located on any public road or right-of-way. 
(4)  Mud control. Mud shall not be carried onto paved public roads by logging vehicles. Where necessary, a temporary construction exit of gravel shall be maintained by the timber harvester to eliminate any hazard to traffic or unsightly conditions on the public right-of-way. 
(5)  Vehicles prohibited on unimproved public roads during inclement weather. During periods of rain or inclement weather, logging vehicles shall not be operated over the unimproved public roads when such travel causes sufficient damage to the road system that the passage of smaller and lighter vehicles is hampered. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 10-28. - Final inspection; notice of damages; effect of failure to repair damages. 
The county road department supervisor shall inspect all affected public property and public rights-of-way to ensure that the same has not been damaged or has been restored to its original condition, including any shaping of ditches, grading or seeding as required. The timber harvester shall be notified in writing of any deficiencies and given 15 business days to correct the deficiencies. If not accomplished during that period, the county road department or its designee shall be authorized to complete the work at the cost of the timber harvester. When the county road department superintendent determines that the road and access site are in a proper state of repair, the superintendent shall provide a written release of liability to the timber harvester. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Secs. 10-29—10-59. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PUBLIC ENTERTAINMENT FACILITIES 

Sec. 10-60. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Dance hall includes any business, establishment, facility or other entity, where one of its purposes is promoting, facilitating, conducting or permitting public dancing on its premises. 
Entertainment means any musical or dance performance, live or recorded, theatrical performance, literary reading or disc jockey performance where the audience is present at the actual time of the occurrence or performance. Without limiting the generality of the foregoing, and except as otherwise excepted elsewhere herein, a jukebox, tape deck, stereo, sound system, compact disc player, television, video projection, or other means of playing music constitutes entertainment. 
Public entertainment facility or entity means a business, establishment, enterprise, or facility, or any organization, located within the unincorporated area of the county that provides music, dancing or entertainment of any nature, except as specifically exempt herein. 
(Ord. of 6-5-2007, § II) 
Sec. 10-61. - Prohibited hours. 
It is unlawful for any public entertainment facility or entity located within the unincorporated area of the county to offer or provide public entertainment between the hours of midnight and 6:00 a.m. Further, all public entertainment facilities located within the unincorporated area of the county shall be closed and cleared of all persons by 1:00 a.m. on Sunday and shall not resume business any earlier than 6:00 a.m. the following Monday morning, and shall be closed and cleared of all persons by 1:00 a.m. on all other days. 
(Ord. of 6-5-2007, § III) 
Sec. 10-62. - Parking. 
Every entertainment facility must have adequate parking for all of its guests, customers, patrons and employees either on its own premises or at such other locations where the facility or business is authorized to park vehicles. Owners, operators, managers, temporary users, tenants and lessees of entertainment facilities shall be responsible for providing adequate parking for the facility's respective guests, customers, patrons and employees, and shall not permit any of their guests, customers, patrons or employees, to remain in or on the subject facility's premises unless such persons are parked on the premises or at such off-premises locations as the owner, operator, manager, temporary user, tenant or lessee of the facility has permission for persons attending the facility to park, or at locations authorized for public parking during the times the facility is open for business. 
(Ord. of 6-5-2007, § IV) 
Sec. 10-63. - Safety and security; noise restricted near occupied residences. 
(a)  Security personnel. Every owner, operator, manager, temporary user, tenant or lessee of a public entertainment facility shall provide adequate security to ensure the safety and welfare of persons attending the facility, or events at the facility in such numbers as is reasonably necessary to protect the health, safety and welfare of those persons at the facility during its hours of operation. At a minimum, each facility must have at least one security person on duty for each 100 persons present during the facility's hours of operation when music is being played or when dancing is permitted. 
(b)  Maximum capacity fire rating. Each facility providing public entertainment must be rated by a state fire marshal or the local fire department for the maximum number of persons which may be in the facility at any given time. A copy of the maximum capacity shall be posted in each public entertainment facility. The owner, operator, manager, temporary user, tenant or lessee of each public entertainment facility shall be responsible for limiting the number of persons at any given time to the approved maximum capacity for the facility. Failure to restrict the number of persons in the facility to the maximum capacity established by the fire marshal or local fire department shall be a violation of this article. if no maximum capacity sign is currently posted in a facility it shall be the responsibility of the owner, operator, tenant, lessee or manager to obtain and post such sign. 
(c)  Noise control. Each entertainment facility subject to this article which is located within 1,000 feet of any occupied residence must keep all exterior doors and windows closed anytime music is being played in order to help keep the music and noise from inside the facility from being an annoyance or nuisance to persons not on the premises or attending the facility. The 1,000-foot distance shall be measured from the point on the facility building nearest the residence. 
(d)  Adequate ventilation. In coordination with the noise control requirements, each entertainment facility must also provide adequate ventilation by air conditioning, fans, or other means for the health and safety of those persons in the facility. 
(Ord. of 6-5-2007, § V) 
Sec. 10-64. - Prosecution of violations; penalties. 
(a)  Every person, whether acting as an individual owner, temporary user, tenant, lessee, employee of any owner or operator for an owner, or whether acting as an agent or independent contractor for the owner, employee, operator, temporary user, tenant or lessee unless specifically exempted or excluded elsewhere herein, who participates in or allows, directly or indirectly, the operation of a public entertainment facility in violation of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor offense hereunder, and upon conviction, shall be punishable by a maximum fine not to exceed $500.00 or by imprisonment in the county jail not to exceed 180 days or both. 
(b)  Notwithstanding the foregoing, anyone violating this article upon the first offense shall be given a written warning, a copy of which shall be filed with the county sheriff's department and retained for a period of five years. 
(c)  Summons for violations of this article shall be issued by the county sheriff's department and shall be returnable to the state court of the county for trial and disposition. The state court of the county shall have the jurisdiction to try all cases involving a violation of this article. 
(d)  Each day any violation of this article occurs shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 6-5-2007, § VI) 
Sec. 10-65. - Exemptions and exclusions. 
No activity that constitutes constitutionally protected speech or any other activity that is protected by the federal or state constitutions is prohibited by this article. In addition, this article does not apply to the following: 
(1)  Any activities or entertainment carried on in an individual's home or residence providing attendees are not required to pay an admission or cover charge. 
(2)  Any activities which primarily consists of sports events or broadcasts or re-broadcasts of sports events by television, video, or radio, or otherwise, even though some music or dancing is a part of or may be incidentally connected to or integrated into the sports activity or the viewing of such sports activities or events. 
(3)  Any school or school-related function, dance, prom, homecoming or other activity officially sponsored or sanctioned by the county board of education, school administration or any organization officially recognized or sanctioned by the county board of education or school administration. 
(4)  Church or other religious activities and events that have as their primary purpose church or religious related goals, and other events organized or sponsored by recognized charitable organizations, where dancing and playing music during the prohibited hours is only nominal and is not a main part or primary goal of the activity or event. Without limiting the generality of the foregoing, church sponsored overnight youth activities, retreats and revivals would constitute exempt activities. 
(Ord. of 6-5-2007, § VIII) 
Sec. 10-66. - Variances. 
(a)  Persons eligible. Any charitable, family, religious, civic or non-profit organization that desires to conduct an activity referenced in this article during the times prohibited by this article may apply to the county board of commissioners for a variance not to exceed three consecutive calendar days in a 12-month period. Variances are not required for entertainment activities unless they are scheduled to take place during the times prohibited by this article. 
(b)  Limitations. No organization may obtain more than one variance within any consecutive 12-month period. Variances may be allowed for entertainment activities to continue for a reasonable time, but not later than 3:00 a.m. 
(c)  Application content and filing. An application for a variance must include the name, address and type of organization, the dates and times of the activity, the nature of entertainment, and the location of the proposed activity. The application must be submitted to the office of the board of county commissioners no less than 120 days prior to the first day of the proposed activity or event for which the variance is requested. There is no fee for filing an application for a variance, except the actual cost of the legal ad referenced above. 
(d)  Publication of notice of application for variance. When an application for a variance is filed, a legal notice of such application shall be published for two consecutive weeks in the county newspaper in which sheriff's sales are advertised, with the first such publication to be within ten days after the date the application is received by the board of commissioners. 
(e)  Objections to variance. Any person have any objection to the application for variance must file his objection in writing and such written objection must be received in the office of the board of county commissioners no later than the 20th day after the day the first notice is published. 
(f)  Consideration by board; final determination. The board of commissioners must meet to consider and vote on the variance application no earlier than the 40th day and not later than the 60th day after the date the application for variance is received in the board's office. The board will make a determination on the application no later than 60 days after the application is received, and may either grant or deny the application, or grant the application in part or with limitations or modifications. 
(g)  Criteria for consideration. The board shall consider, in evaluating each application, the dates and times requested; the proposed location and its proximity to residences and residential areas; and whether the proposed activity will pose any serious threat to the health, safety or welfare of the general public. 
(Ord. of 6-5-2007, § IX) 
Secs. 10-67—10-90. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - TATTOO AND BODY PIERCING 

Sec. 10-91. - Board of health rules adopted. 
The rules and regulations of the county board of health with regard to tattoo and body piercing studios and artists as amended from time to time are adopted as though fully set forth in this article. A copy of such rules and regulations are available from the county board of health and in the office of the county clerk. 
Sec. 10-92. - Enforcement and penalties. 
Enforcement of the adopted rules and regulations shall be in accordance with O.C.G.A. ch. 31-5. The county board of health is authorized to enforce the provisions of this article. 
(Ord. of 4-8-2004, § XXIII) 
Chapter 12 - EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT AND SERVICES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Emergency management generally, O.C.G.A. § 38-3-1 et seq.; local organizations for emergency management, O.C.G.A. § 38-3-27; authority to promulgate local rules and regulations, O.C.G.A. § 38-3-28; mutual aid, O.C.G.A. § 36-69-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 12-1—12-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT AND RESPONSE 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 12-19. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Curfew means a regulation prohibiting the appearance and presence of any person not otherwise exempt under the provisions of this chapter or state law in certain public areas during specified hours. 
Disaster means any natural, technological, civil emergency or threat thereof that causes or has the potential to cause damage of sufficient severity and magnitude to result in a declaration of a state of emergency declared by a county, the state governor or the president of the United States. 
Emergency means any natural or manmade event requiring the activation of the local emergency operations plan. 
Emergency management means the preparation for the carrying out of all emergency functions, other than functions for which military forces are primarily responsible, to prevent, minimize, and repair injury and damage resulting from emergencies, energy emergencies, disasters, or the imminent threat thereof, of manmade or natural origin, caused by enemy attack, sabotage, acts of domestic or international terrorism, civil disturbance, fire, flood, earthquake, wind, storm, wave action, oil spill or other water contamination, requiring emergency action to avert danger or damage, epidemic, air contamination, blight, drought, infestation, explosion, riot or other hostile action, radiological action, or other causes. These functions include, without limitation: 
(1)  Firefighting services; 
(2)  Police services; emergency medical services; 
(3)  Rescue; 
(4)  Engineering; 
(5)  Warning services; 
(6)  Communications; 
(7)  Defense from radiological, chemical, biological, and other special weapons to include weapons of mass destruction; 
(8)  Evacuation of persons from stricken areas; 
(9)  Emergency welfare services; 
(10)  Consequence management functions to include victim services; 
(11)  Emergency transportation; 
(12)  Plant protection; 
(13)  Temporary restoration of public utility services; and 
(14)  Other functions related to civilian protection, together with all other activities necessary or incidental to the preparation for and carrying out of the foregoing functions. 
Fees means any fee or rate charged by the county for building permits, land disturbance permits, zoning applications, special land use permits, temporary land use permits, and other fees relating to the reconstruction, repair and clean up of areas impacted by the disaster or emergency. The term "fees" does not include those fees collected by the county on behalf of the federal or state government or those fees charged by the county pursuant to a federal or state statute or regulation. 
Local emergency means the existence of conditions of extreme peril to the safety of persons and property within the territorial limits of the county caused by natural disasters, riots, civil disturbances, or other situations presenting major law enforcement and other public safety problems, which conditions are or are likely to be beyond the control of the services, personnel, equipment, and facilities of that political subdivision of the state and which require the combined forces of other political subdivisions of the state to combat. 
Local emergency management director means the person nominated by the local governments and appointed by the state emergency management director to implement the local emergency operations plan. 
State of emergency means a condition declared by the governor, or by an authorized local governing official pursuant to authority granted in this chapter or by state law, when in his judgment the threat or actual occurrence disaster, emergency, or energy emergency is of sufficient severity and magnitude to warrant extraordinary efforts in preventing or alleviating the damage, loss, hardship, or suffering threatened or caused thereby. 
State emergency management director means the person appointed by the governor to head the state emergency management agency. 
Subsequent recovery period means the period of time that the disaster emergency continues to cause disruptions in the area impacted by the disaster emergency. The subsequent recovery period shall not exceed six months after a state of emergency declaration is terminated unless extended by official action of the governing authority of the county. 
Temporary dwelling means any mobile or easily movable home, trailer, recreational vehicle as well as any other structure not otherwise permitted by the zoning regulations in a particular zoning district, or any other non-permanent structure used in lieu of permanent structure that has been damaged or destroyed. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(1), § I; Ord. of 4-1-2008(2), § 2; Ord. of 4-1-2008(3), § 2) 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. §§ 38-3-3, 36-69-2. 
Secs. 12-20—12-41. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT AGENCY AND PLAN[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Authority for local rules and regulations for emergency management, O.C.G.A. § 38-3-28; local director required for state financial assistance, O.C.G.A. § 38-3-27; authority for nomination of local director of emergency management, O.C.G.A. § 38-3-27. 

Sec. 12-42. - Joint local organization for emergency management established. 
In agreement with the governing officials of the cities within the county, there is herby established the Jeff Davis Emergency Management Agency. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(1), § II(intro.)) 
Sec. 12-43. - Nomination of local director; duties. 
(a)  The chairperson of the county commissioners, with the concurrence of officials of the cities within the county, shall nominate, for appointment by the state emergency management director, a director of the county emergency management agency. 
(b)  Upon appointment, the local emergency management agency director shall have direct responsibility for the organization, administration, and operations of the local organization for emergency management, subject to the direction and control of the executive officer or governing body and shall serve at the pleasure of such executive officer or governing body. 
(c)  When appointed, the local emergency management director is charged with the following duties: 
(1)  Represent the governing officials of the county on matters pertaining to emergency management. 
(2)  Assist local officials in organizing county departments for emergency operations. 
(3)  Develop, in conjunction with county and city departments, the county emergency operations plan for emergency functions. Such plan will be in consonance with the state emergency operations plan and shall be submitted to the governing officials of the county and the cities within the county for approval, and thence to the state emergency management agency for approval. 
(4)  Maintain the emergency management agency and carry out the day-to-day administration of the county emergency management program, including the submission of required reports, to the state emergency management agency. 
(5)  Submit reports as required by governmental officials in keeping with good management practices (e.g., financial, daily activities, etc.). 
(6)  Obtain, with the authority of governing officials, a facility to be used as the county emergency operations center. 
(7)  Coordinate the activities of the county emergency operating staff during periods of emergency, and under the supervision of county governing officials. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(1), § II(intro.), (a)-(g)) 
State Law reference— Authority for nomination of local director of emergency management, O.C.G.A. § 38-3-27. 
Sec. 12-44. - Assignment of emergency functions. 
(a)  The county emergency management agency shall be established around existing county and city departments. The emergency support functions and department and agency assignments are as follows: 

 
(b)  Heads of county departments listed in the table in subsection (a) of this section are responsible for developing appropriate annexes and standard operating procedures to the emergency operations plan for their assigned emergency functions. Such annexes and standard operating procedures will be submitted to the emergency management director for inclusion in the local emergency operations plan for submission to appropriate local officials for approval. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(1), § III) 
Sec. 12-45. - Emergency powers of county board chairperson and mayors. 
In the event of a manmade or natural disaster or any other emergency which may effect the lives and property of the citizens of the county, the chairperson of the county board of commissioners separately, or jointly with the mayor of the City of Hazlehurst and the City of Denton or in their legally appointed successors, may determine that an emergency or disaster exists and thereafter shall have and may exercise for such periods as such emergency or disaster continues power to: 
(1)  Appropriate and expend funds, execute contracts, and to obtain and distribute equipment, materials, and supplies for emergency management purposes; 
(2)  Provide for the health and safety of persons and property, including emergency assistance to the victims of any emergency or disaster resulting from manmade or natural causes or enemy attack and to direct and coordinate the development of emergency management plans and programs in accordance with the policies and plans set by the federal and state emergency management agencies; 
(3)  Appoint, employ, remove, or provide, with or without compensation, chiefs of services, warning personnel, rescue teams, auxiliary fire and police personnel, and other emergency management workers; 
(4)  Establish a primary and one or more secondary control centers to serve as command posts during an emergency or disaster; 
(5)  Subject to the order of the governor or the chief executive of the political subdivision, assign and make available for duty the employees, property, or equipment of the subdivision relating to firefighting, engineering, rescue, health, medical and related services, and to police, transportation, construction, and similar items or services for emergency management purposes, within or outside of the physical limits of the subdivision; 
(6)  Acquire, temporarily or permanently, by purchase, lease, or otherwise, sites required for installation of temporary housing units for disaster victims; and to enter into whatever arrangements, including purchase, of temporary housing units and payment of transportation charges, which are necessary to prepare or equip such sites to utilize the housing units. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(1), § IV) 
Sec. 12-46. - Volunteers. 
All persons, other than officers and employees of the county, performing emergency functions pursuant to this article, may serve with or without compensation. While engaged in such emergency functions, duly assigned volunteers shall have the same immunities as county officers and employees; provided, however, that immunity does not apply in cases of willful misconduct, gross negligence or bad faith. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(1), § V) 
Sec. 12-47. - Violations and penalties. 
Any violation of any provision of this division or any rule, order or regulation made pursuant to this article, shall upon conviction be punished as a misdemeanor. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(1), § VI) 
Secs. 12-48—12-67. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - ALTERNATIVE REGULATIONS DURING EMERGENCY 

Sec. 12-68. - Relocation of government meetings and other conduct of business. 
Upon proclamation by the appropriate state official of an emergency or disaster of manmade or natural causes or enemy attack impending on or affecting state or the United States, the affairs and business of the county may be conducted at places other than the regular or usual place thereof, within or outside of the county, when it is not prudent, expedient or possible to conduct business at the regular location. When such meetings occur outside of county, all actions taken by the local governing body shall be as valid and binding as if performed within the county. Such meetings may be called by the presiding officer or any two members of the governing body without regard to or compliance with time-consuming procedures and formalities otherwise required by law. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(2), § 1(1)) 
Sec. 12-69. - Purchasing and public works contracts. 
Upon the declaration of a state of emergency by the governor, or upon the determination by the county board of commissioners, or its designee, of the existence of an emergency or disaster, the county board of commissioners, their designee or the emergency interim successor may contract for public works without letting such contract out to the lowest, responsible bidder and without advertising and posting notification of such contract for four weeks; provided, however, that any public works contract entered into pursuant to this subsection shall be entered on the minutes of the county as soon as practical and the nature of the emergency described therein. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(2), § 1(2)) 
Sec. 12-70. - Code enforcement. 
Upon the declaration of a state of emergency by the governor, or upon the determination by the county board of commissioners, or its designee, of the existence of an emergency or disaster, the county board of commissioners, their designee or the emergency interim successor may temporarily suspend the enforcement of this Code or any portion thereof, if the emergency or disaster is of such nature that immediate action outside the Code is required, such suspension is consistent with the protection of the public health, safety and welfare, and such suspension is not inconsistent with any federal or state statutes or regulations. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(2), § 1(3)) 
Sec. 12-71. - Fees. 
Upon the declaration of a state of emergency by the governor, or upon the determination by the county board of commissioners, or its designee, of the existence of an emergency or disaster, the county board of commissioners, their designee or the emergency interim successor may temporarily reduce or suspend any permit fees, application fees or other rate structures as necessary to encourage the rebuilding of the area impacted by the disaster or emergency. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(2), § 1(4)) 
Sec. 12-72. - Temporary dwellings. 
Upon the declaration of a state of emergency by the governor, or upon the determination by the county board of commissioners, or its designee, of the existence of an emergency or disaster, the county board of commissioners, their designee or the emergency interim successor may issue temporary mobile home, trailer, recreational vehicle or other temporary dwelling structures or parks in any zoning district while the primary dwelling is being repaired provided that such temporary dwellings or parks are designed by an engineer or other person deemed qualified by the county sovereign authority and the plans are approved by the county health department and the county building and inspections department, or other persons deemed qualified by the counties sovereign authority to approve such plan. The temporary permit shall not exceed six months in duration. In the case of continuing hardship and in the discretion of the governing authority or its designee, the permit may be extended for a period for an additional six months. Upon expiration of the temporary permit or an extension, the temporary dwelling shall be removed. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(2), § 1(5)) 
Secs. 12-73—12-102. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - EMERGENCY CURFEW 

Sec. 12-103. - Institution and applicability. 
Upon the declaration of a state of emergency by the governor, or upon the determination by the county chairperson or his designee, of the existence of an emergency or disaster, the county board of commissioners, its designee or the emergency interim successor may adopt a resolution instituting a curfew when it is determined necessary to protect and safeguard the people and property of the county. The resolution instituting the curfew shall include the dates and hours that the curfew shall be in effect. All of the territory of the unincorporated county shall be subject to the terms of the curfew, unless otherwise specified in the resolution. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(3), § 1) 
Sec. 12-104. - Compliance with curfew required; places in which presence is prohibited. 
It shall be prohibited for any person, other than exempt individuals, to appear in public in the territory subject to the curfew, including, but not limited to, streets, highways, alleys, sidewalks, vacant lots, parks, public buildings or any other public places in all or a delineated part of unincorporated the county during the stated hours of the curfew. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(3), § 3) 
Sec. 12-105. - Persons exempt from curfew. 
Unless otherwise specified in the resolution implementing the curfew, individuals engaged in the provision of designated, essential services, such as fire, law enforcement, emergency medical services and hospital services, military services, utility emergency repairs. The curfew resolution may, in the discretion of the governing authority, also exempt regular employees of local industries traveling to and from their jobs with appropriate identification, news media employees, properly registered and licensed building and repair contractors performing activities related to construction, repair, renovation or improvement of buildings and other structures damaged during the disaster or emergency. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(3), § 2) 
Sec. 12-106. - Penalties. 
Any individual violating this division, upon conviction, shall be punishable by a fine not to exceed $1,000.00 per violation or imprisonment not to exceed 60 days, or both. 
(Ord. of 4-1-2008(3), § 4) 
Secs. 12-107—12-125. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - AMBULANCE SERVICES 

Sec. 12-126. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Advance life support means the provision of care and procedures included in the paramedic courses and scope of practice, as approved by the state department of human resources. 
Advanced life support ambulance means an ambulance with adequate equipment, supplies, and pharmaceuticals to provide advanced life support care as outlined in the paramedic curriculum and the paramedic scope of practice, as approved by the state department of human resources. An advanced life support ambulance must be staffed by two state certified emergency medical technicians, one of whom must be a state licensed paramedic at all times. As a minimum, an advanced life support ambulance must be equipped with a cardiac monitor with external defibrillation/pacing and a transport ventilator. 
Nonemergency transport service means a patient transport service that strictly limits its service exclusively to the transport of non-emergency patients. 
Paramedic means a person currently licensed by the state department of human resources as an emergency medical technician-paramedic. 
Point of origin means the location where the patient to be transported is located or the location from which the patient is to be picked up by the ambulance service. 
(Ord. of 9-24-2008, § 1) 
Sec. 12-127. - Administration, inspection, and compliance. 
(a)  The county administrator or his designee shall serve as administrator of this article for the purposes of inspection and approving compliance. 
(b)  Each ambulance service covered by this article must provide a letter outlining compliance with this article prior to engaging in services covered by this article; failure to do so will be a violation of this article. A sample letter may be provided by the county administrator. 
(c)  Every ambulance service covered by this article may be inspected at any time, with or without prior notice, to ensure compliance with this article. The inspection may include an inspection of ambulance, equipment, supplies, and credentials of personnel. Inspections shall be made by the county administrator or the administrator's designee for the purpose of enforcing compliance. 
(d)  A copy of this article (and any future amendments) will be furnished by the administrator or his designee to each ambulance service subject to this article. 
(Ord. of 9-24-2008, § 2) 
Sec. 12-128. - Applicability. 
Except as otherwise provided in this article, this article shall apply to any ambulance service being offered or furnished to any point of origin within the boundaries of the county and to all ambulance services having a base of operation in the county or having ambulances stationed in the county. 
(Ord. of 9-24-2008, § 3) 
Sec. 12-129. - Exempt services. 
(a)  Any ambulance service being operated by an agency of the federal government or ambulance service being provided under a direct contract with the federal government, if request for such service is made by the federal government, is exempt from this article. 
(b)  Any ambulance service temporarily rendering assistance in the case of a catastrophe or emergency in which the capabilities of local services operating in the county are exceeded or an ambulance service being provided under a valid mutual aid agreement is exempt from this article. 
(c)  Any ambulance service providing inter-facility neonatal transportation services is exempt from this article. 
(d)  This article shall not apply to non-emergency transport services which limit their services exclusively to the transport of non-emergency patients. 
(Ord. of 9-24-2008, § 4) 
Sec. 12-130. - General operational regulations. 
(a)  All ambulance services, ambulances, and personnel shall at all times, be operated in compliance with all county, state and federal laws, rules, regulations, ordinances. 
(b)  All ambulance services being offered to a point of origin within this county shall be capable of providing advanced life support utilizing an advanced life support ambulance. 
(c)  In addition to providing advanced life support, all primary duty ambulances shall be equipped and have full-time personnel trained to provide adult and pediatric intra-osseous IV access. 
(d)  Any ambulance service offering services for point of origin within this county shall staff a primary duty ambulance and be available 24 hours a day, seven days a week. 
(e)  If the primary duty ambulance engages in inter-facility transports to destinations outside of the county, then the provider must provide a second backup ambulance staffed in the same manner as required for the primary duty ambulance, located within the limits of this county with the capability to respond in no more than 30 minutes to a local request for ambulance service. Backup ambulances are required to provide advanced life support utilizing an advanced life support ambulance. Back up ambulances are exempt from the requirements in subsection (c) of this section. 
(f)  Any ambulance service offering service for points of origin within the county must have a permanent base of operation located within the county and a local or toll-free number for service requests. 
(g)  All ambulance services offering services for points of origin within the county must not advertise or encourage the use of any other telephone number other than 9-1-1 for emergency calls. 
(Ord. of 9-24-2008, § 5) 
Sec. 12-131. - Indemnification and insurance. 
(a)  Each person, firm, or corporation owning or operating an ambulance service within this county shall save, defend, indemnify and hold harmless the county and all residents of the county for any loss or damage caused by, or resulting from the operations of, the ambulance service. 
(b)  Each privately owned ambulance service must have and keep in force at all times a general liability insurance policy with limits of not less than $1,000,000.00 which covers both patients being transported and third parties. A copy of such policy must be provided to the county administrator or his designee prior to beginning service in this county; and each ambulance service subject to the ordinance shall provide the county administrator with a copy of each renewal of the policy. Failure to keep such a policy in force at all times will be a violation of this article. 
(Ord. of 9-24-2008, § 6) 
Sec. 12-132. - Penalty. 
The maximum fine for any ambulance service found in violation of this article shall be $1,000.00 per occurrence. The maximum fine for any individual person found in violation of this article shall be $250.00 per occurrence. 
(Ord. of 9-24-2008, § 7) 
Secs. 12-133—12-162. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - 9-1-1 COMMUNICATIONS SURCHARGES[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference— Georgia Emergency Telephone Number 9-1-1 Service Act of 1977, O.C.G.A. § 46-5-120 et seq. 

Sec. 12-163. - Wireless telecommunications. 
The county imposes a 9-1-1 charge of $1.50 per month per wireless connection provided to each telephone subscriber whose billing address is within the jurisdiction of the county. 
(Res. of 7-10-1997; Res. of 10-8-1998; Res. of 11-9-2006) 
Sec. 12-164. - Voice over internet protocol (VoIP). 
The county imposes a 9-1-1 charge of $1.50 per month on each voice over internet protocol telecommunications connection (VoIP) subscribed to by subscribers whose billing address is within the jurisdiction of the county. 
(Res. of 10-16-2008) 
Sec. 12-165. - Prepaid wireless service. 
(a)  Levied. Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 46-5-134.2, the county imposes a prepaid wireless 9-1-1 charge of $0.75 on every prepaid wireless retail transaction occurring within the jurisdiction of the public safety answering point as such term is defined in O.C.G.A. § 46-5-122. 
(b)  Collection. Prepaid wireless 9-1-1 charges collected by sellers shall be remitted to the commissioner of the state department of revenue at the times and in the manner provided by O.C.G.A. ch. 48-8 (State Sales and Use Taxes, O.C.G.A. § 48-8-1 et seq.) respect to the sales and use tax imposed on prepaid wireless calling service. 
(c)  Disposition of funds. Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 46-5-134.20(5), funds received by the county from charges imposed by this section shall be deposited in the emergency telephone system fund maintained by the county pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 46-5-134 and kept separate from general revenue of the county, and all such funds shall be used exclusively for the purposes authorized by O.C.G.A. § 46-5-134(e). 
(Res. of 6-20-2011) 
Chapter 14 - ENVIRONMENT[1]

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 14-1—14-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - SOIL EROSION AND SEDIMENTATION[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Control of soil erosion and sedimentation, O.C.G.A. § 12-7-1 et seq. 

Secs. 14-19—14-39. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 14-40. - Definitions. 
The following definitions shall apply in the interpretation and enforcement of this article, unless otherwise specifically stated: 
Best management practices (BMPs) means a collection of structural practices and vegetative measures that when properly designed, installed and maintained, will provide effective erosion and sedimentation control for all rainfall events up to and including a 25-year, 24-hour rainfall event. 
Board means the state board of natural resources. 
Buffer means the area of land immediately adjacent to the banks of state waters in its natural state of vegetation, which facilitates the protection of water quality and aquatic habitat. 
Commission means the state soil and water conservation commission. 
Cut and excavation means a portion of land surface or area from which earth has been removed or will be removed by excavation; the depth below original ground surface to excavated surface. 
Department means the state department of natural resources. 
Director means the director of the environmental protection division of the state department of natural resources. 
District means the Altamaha Soil and Water Conservation District. 
Division means the environmental protection division of the state department of natural resources. 
Drainage structure means a device composed of a virtually nonerodible material such as concrete, steel, plastic or other such material that conveys water from one place to another by intercepting the flow and carrying it to a release point for stormwater management, drainage control, or flood control purposes. 
Erosion means the process by which land surface is worn away by the action of wind, water, ice or gravity. 
Erosion and sedimentation control plan means a plan for the control of soil erosion and sedimentation resulting from a land disturbing activity. 
Fill means a portion of land surface to which soil or other solid material has been added and refers to the depth above the original ground. 
Finished grade means the final elevation and contour of the ground after cutting or filling and conforming to the proposed design. 
Grading means altering the shape of ground surfaces to a predetermined condition; this includes stripping, cutting, filling, stockpiling and shaping or any combination thereof and shall include the land in its cut or filled condition. 
Ground elevation means the original elevation of the ground surface prior to cutting or filling. 
Issuing authority means the governing authority of any county or municipality that has been certified by the director of the environmental protection division of the state department of natural resources as an issuing authority, pursuant to the O.C.G.A. § 12-7-8(a) or the division in those instances where an application for a permit is submitted to the division. 
Land disturbing activity means any activity which may result in soil erosion from water or wind and the movement of sediments into state waters or onto lands within the state, including, but not limited to, clearing, dredging, grading, excavating, transporting, and filling of land but not including agricultural practices as described in this article. 
Metropolitan River Protection Act (MRPA) means a state law referenced as O.C.G.A. § 12-5-440 et seq. that addresses environmental and developmental matters in certain metropolitan river corridors and their drainage basins. 
Natural ground surface means the ground surface in its original state before any grading, excavation or filling. 
Nephelometric turbidity units (NTU) means numerical units of measure based upon photometric analytical techniques for measuring the light scattered by finely divided particles of a substance in suspension. This technique is used to estimate the extent of turbidity in water in which colloidally dispersed particles are present. 
Permit means the authorization necessary to conduct a land disturbing activity under the provisions of this article. 
Person means any individual, partnership, firm, association, joint venture, public or private corporation, trust, estate, commission, board, public or private institution, utility, cooperative, state agency, municipality or other political subdivision of this state, any interstate body or any other legal entity. 
Plan means the county erosion and sedimentation control plan. 
Project means the entire proposed development project regardless of the size of the area of land to be disturbed. 
Roadway drainage structure means a device such as a bridge, culvert, or ditch, composed of a virtually nonerodible material such as concrete, steel, plastic, or other such material that conveys water under a roadway by intercepting the flow on one side of a traveled way consisting of one or more defined lanes, with or without shoulder areas, and carrying water to a release point on the other side. 
Sediment means solid material, both organic and inorganic, that is in suspension, is being transported, or has been moved from its site of origin by air, water, ice, or gravity as a product of erosion. 
Sedimentation means the process by which eroded material is transported and deposited by the action of water, wind, ice or gravity. 
Soil and water conservation district approved plan means an erosion and sedimentation control plan approved in writing by the Altamaha Soil and Water Conservation District. 
Stabilization means the process of establishing an enduring soil cover of vegetation by the installation of temporary or permanent structures for the purpose of reducing to a minimum the erosion process and the resultant transport of sediment by wind, water, ice or gravity. 
State waters means any and all rivers, streams, creeks, branches, lakes, reservoirs, ponds, drainage systems, springs, wells, and other bodies of surface or subsurface water, natural or artificial, lying within or forming a part of the boundaries of the state that are not entirely confined and retained completely upon the property of a single individual, partnership, or corporation. 
Structural erosion and sedimentation control practices means practices for the stabilization of erodible or sediment-producing areas by utilizing the mechanical properties of matter for the purpose of either changing the surface of the land or storing, regulating or disposing of runoff to prevent excessive sediment loss. Examples of structural erosion and sediment control practices are riprap, sediment basins, dikes, level spreaders, waterways or outlets, diversions, grade stabilization structures, sediment traps and land grading, etc. 
Trout streams means all streams or portions of streams within the watershed as designated by the game and fish division of the state department of natural resources under the provisions of the Georgia Water Quality Control Act, O.C.G.A. § 12-5-20 et seq. 
(1)  The term "primary trout water" means streams which water is capable of supporting a self-sustaining population of rainbow, brown or brook trout. 
(2)  The term "secondary trout water" means streams in which there is no evidence of natural trout reproduction, but are capable of supporting trout throughout the year. 
(3)  The term "first order trout waters" means streams into which no other streams flow except springs. 
Vegetative erosion and sedimentation control measures means measures for the stabilization of erodible or sediment-producing areas by covering the soil with: 
(1)  Permanent seeding, sprigging or planting, producing long-term vegetative cover; 
(2)  Temporary seeding, producing short-term vegetative cover; or 
(3)  Sodding, covering areas with a turf of perennial sod-forming grass. 
Watercourse means any natural or artificial watercourse, stream, river, creek, channel, ditch, canal, conduit, culvert, drain, waterway, gully, ravine, or wash in which water flows either continuously or intermittently and that has a definite channel, bed and banks, and including any area adjacent thereto subject to inundation by reason of overflow or floodwater. 
Wetlands means those areas that are inundated or saturated by surface water or groundwater at a frequency and duration sufficient to support, and that under normal circumstances do support a prevalence of vegetation typically adapted for life in saturated soil conditions. The term "wetlands," generally, include swamps, marshes, bogs, and similar areas. 
Sec. 14-41. - Exemptions. 
(a)  This article shall apply to any land disturbing activity undertaken by any person on any land except for the following: 
(1)  Surface mining, as the same is defined in the Georgia Surface Mining Act of 1968, O.C.G.A. § 12-4-70 et seq.; 
(2)  Granite quarrying and land clearing for such quarrying; 
(3)  Such minor land disturbing activities as home gardens and individual home landscaping, repairs, maintenance work, fences, and other related activities which result in minor soil erosion; 
(4)  The construction of single-family residences, when such construction disturbs less than one acre and is not a part of a larger common plan of development or sale with a planned disturbance of equal to or greater than one acre and not otherwise exempted under this subsection; provided, however, that construction of any such residence shall conform to the minimum requirements as set forth in O.C.G.A. § 12-7-6 and this subsection; 
a.  For single-family residence construction covered by the provisions of this subsection (a)(4), there shall be a buffer zone between the residence and any state waters classified as trout streams pursuant to the Georgia Water Quality Control Act, O.C.G.A. § 12-5-20 et seq. In any such buffer zone, no land disturbing activity shall be constructed between the residence and the point where vegetation has been wrested by normal stream flow or wave action from the banks of the trout waters; 
b.  For primary trout waters, the buffer zone shall be at least 50 horizontal feet, and no variance to a smaller buffer shall be granted. For secondary trout waters, the buffer zone shall be at least 50 horizontal feet, but the director may grant variances to no less than 25 feet;
