Chapter 28 - ROADS, RIGHTS-OF-WAY AND OTHER PUBLIC PLACES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— County road systems, O.C.G.A. § 32-4-40 et seq.; powers of county with regard to roads, O.C.G.A. § 32-4-42; removal of public road obstructions, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-4; obstructing highways prohibited, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-43; construction and maintenance of private roads by local governments prohibited, O.C.G.A. § 32-1-8. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 28-1—28-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - DAMAGE TO COUNTY ROADS 

Sec. 28-19. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Damage means any and all injury to the roadbed, road, surface, ditches, drainage system, or right-of-way of a road which is part of the county public road system. Acts of injury shall include, but not be limited to, the following: 
(1)  Diversion of or the filling in of any drainage ditch, culvert or pipe parallel to or underneath a public road, so as to restrain or redirect the flow of water. 
(2)  The operation of any vehicle, machinery, or equipment which will gouge, rip, break, depress or otherwise deface a public road, its adjoining ditches, or any part of the public right-of-way. 
(3)  The continued ingress or egress, to and from a public road at a particular location which results in a build-up of rock, gravel, mud, dirt, debris or other materials, which present a potential hazard to other persons using the public road. 
(4)  The creation or erection of any dam, berm, ditch or wall which restrains the natural flow of waters and results in the redirecting of the waters onto the road surface or right-of-way of any public road within the county. 
(5)  Any act or acts which interferes with or impedes normal motor vehicle traffic or water flow or run off on or over a county road, ditch or right-of-way in this county, or adversely affects the safety of anyone or any other vehicle using the road, ditch or right-of-way. 
Enforcement officer means the county sheriff, the county road superintendent, or their deputies or designees, and any other law enforcement officer in the county. 
Public road means the entire width of any and all roads and roadway rights-of-way that are a part of the county public road system, as delineated in accordance with the road mapping system of the county, as amended from time to time. All drainage ditches within a county road right-of-way which adjoin or run parallel to, or beneath, a county road are included in the term "public road". 
Repair means the repair of a public road to its condition prior to the occurrence of the damage caused. 
(Ord. of 2-11-1999, § II) 
Sec. 28-20. - Damaging public roads prohibited. 
It is unlawful for any person to damage any public road, or to engage or permit any other person to damage a public road in the county. 
(Ord. of 2-11-1999, § III) 
Sec. 28-21. - Temporary ramps excluded. 
(a)  The temporary placement or construction of a ramp across a ditch for purposes of loading and unloading machinery and equipment, or the removing of timber, crops or other materials or substances shall not constitute a violation of this article, providing that the temporary ramp is placed or constructed so as not to significantly restrain or divert the water flow from the roadbed or restrain or divert the water flow through the ditch on or over which the ramp is placed or constructed. 
(b)  For the temporary ramp to be excluded as a violation of this article the temporary ramp must provide for continued normal water flow either by the installation of an adequate size pipe under the ramp or by some other means; furthermore, the person, company or other entity placing the temporary ramp over the ditch must restore the ditch and right-of-way to same or better condition as the ditch and right-of-way were prior to the placement of the temporary ramp. 
(c)  For purposes of this section, the term "temporary" means a period of time not to exceed ten days, except for the harvesting and removal of timber, in which case the term "temporary" means the reasonable amount of time required to harvest and remove the timber. 
(d)  If a temporary ramp is needed for a period of time in excess of that authorized in subsection (c) of this section, then the person desiring to extend the temporary period shall apply to the county administrator for an extension of time. Upon good cause shown, the county administrator, or in his absence, the county clerk or chairperson of the board of commissioners, may grant a reasonable extension of the period for a temporary ramp. 
(Ord. of 2-11-1999, § VII(a)) 
Sec. 28-22. - Permanent entrance ways excluded. 
(a)  Ramps and culverts constructed as permanent entrance ways are excluded from this article providing they are constructed in such a manner as to not restrain or divert the water flow through the right-of-way and ditch over which the ramp or culvert is constructed to any greater extent than the normal water flow was restricted or restrained prior to construction of the ramp or culvert. 
(b)  Any person or entity desiring to construct a permanent entrance way may, but is not required to, consult with the county road superintendent or engineer, or the county administrator prior to constructing such a permanent entranceway to obtain verification that the proposed entrance way will not constitute a violation of this article. 
(Ord. of 2-11-1999, § VII(b)) 
Sec. 28-23. - Enforcement; violations and penalties. 
(a)  Enforcement officers. This article shall be enforced by the sheriff or any deputy or other law enforcement officer, or any other designated county enforcement officer. 
(b)  Citations. Citations for violations may be issued by any enforcement officer requiring an individual defendant to appear before the magistrate's court of the county at the court's next regularly set court date or such other date as set by the judge of the court. Citations shall be personally served upon the defendant or his authorized agent in accordance with state law. Such citation shall state the time and place at which the accused is to appear for trial, shall identify the offense with which the accused is charged, shall have an identifying number by which it shall be filed with the court, and shall be signed by the officer who completes and serves it. 
(c)  Continuing violations; separate offenses. Each day of a continuing violation may be treated as a separate offense, and a citation may be issued each day a violation exists. Each violation shall constitute a separate offense which may be punished separately. 
(d)  Prosecuting attorney options; accusations. The offender may be tried with or without a prosecuting attorney as well as upon accusations. 
(e)  Penalties. A first conviction of this article within a five-year period shall be punishable by a fine of not less than $100.00, and not more than $500.00, or imprisonment of up to 60 days, or both. Upon a second or subsequent conviction of the offense within a five-year period, such conviction shall be punishable by a fine of not less than $500.00, and not more than $1,000.00, or imprisonment of up to 60 days, or both. Additionally the magistrate may require restitution to repair the damage to the public road or require the defendant to complete community service work to repair the damage to the public road. 
(f)  Court costs. In addition, upon conviction, the offender shall be required to pay all court costs as determined by the magistrate. 
(g)  Arrest before trial; bond. No person accused of violating this article shall be arrested prior to trial, but any defendant who fails to appear for trial shall be arrested thereafter on the warrant of the magistrate, and required to post a bond for his future appearance. 
(h)  Jury trial. There shall be no jury trials in the magistrate court. 
(i)  Remedies not exclusive; civil remedies. Nothing in this article shall prevent the county board of commissioners from bringing any civil action to prevent, correct or abate any violation of this article. No penalty or remedy prescribed herein shall be considered exclusive of any other remedy, but shall be available in addition thereto. 
(Ord. of 2-11-1999, §§ IV, VI) 
Secs. 28-24—28-49. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - STREET NUMBERS 

Sec. 28-50. - Display of street numbers required. 
Every house, mobile home, apartment, business, or other building having a street number assigned to it under the system of numbering in unincorporated the county shall display such number in a readily visible manner and in compliance with the requirements of this article. Mobile home parks shall also be required to have each individual pad or lot number displayed in a readily visible manner and in compliance with the requirements of this article. 
(Ord. of 8-12-1999, § 1) 
Sec. 28-51. - Method of display. 
(a)  Assigned street numbers may be affixed to the house, apartment, business or other building itself, provided that such house, apartment, business or other building is not more than 50 feet from the curbline, pavement edge, or edge of travel way of the street in front of the house, apartment, business, or other building, and the number is readily visible from the street by persons traveling along the street in each direction. Street numbers may also be placed on mailboxes or signs located on the premises in front of the house, apartment, business or other building provided such signs are of a durable type and are located not more than 50 feet from the curbline, pavement edge, or edge of travel way of the street in front of the property, and provided that the numbers on such sign shall be readily visible from the street by persons traveling along the street in each direction. 
(b)  If the house, apartment, business or other building to be numbered is more than 50 feet from the curb, pavement edge, or edge of travel way of the street in front of the property, or if for any reason a street number affixed to the building would not be readily visible from the street by persons traveling along the street in each direction, the street number shall not be displayed on the building, but must be displayed on a sign or mailbox complying with the requirements of this article. 
(Ord. of 8-12-1999, § 2) 
Sec. 28-52. - Size and design of numbers. 
Street numbers affixed to buildings or signs shall be a minimum of three inches in height. Those affixed to mailboxes shall be a minimum of two inches in height. All such numbers shall be of a color contrasting to the background so as to be clearly visible. Street numbers and signs or mailboxes to which they are affixed shall be maintained at all times in good condition. 
(Ord. of 8-12-1999, § 3) 
Sec. 28-53. - Duty of owner; violations. 
(a)  The obligation of complying with the provisions of this article shall be upon the owner of the property. The property owner shall have 30 days from the date of notification of his number to comply with the provisions herein. 
(b)  If any of the provisions of this article shall be found to have been violated, notice shall be given to the owner of the property, or his agent, specifying the manner of the violation, and giving the owner ten days to bring the property into compliance. The notice shall be given by the E-911 office. 
(c)  Violation of this article shall be punishable as a misdemeanor pursuant to state statute governing the violation of county ordinances. The maximum penalty for violation of this article shall be a fine not to exceed $100.00. Each day a violation of this article continues after the expiration of the ten-day period shall constitute a separate offense, and shall be punishable as provided by law. 
(Ord. of 8-12-1999, § 4) 
Secs. 28-54—28-79. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - CONNECTING TO PUBLIC ROADS 

Sec. 28-80. - Applicability. 
This article shall apply to the construction of both temporary and permanent non-public ramps, drives and roadways if they are to be joined or connected with a public road. This article does not apply to the construction or improvement of non-public roadways and drives that are not to become, to be joined to or connected with a public road or street. 
(Ord. of 6-12-1984, §§ 13, 14) 
Sec. 28-81. - Penalties for violation. 
Violators of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction of any such violation shall be punished by a fine of not more than $200.00 or 90 days imprisonment for such violation. 
(Ord. of 6-12-1984, § 12) 
Sec. 28-82. - Written permission required to connect ramp, drive or roadway to public road. 
It is unlawful for any person, corporation or other entity to join or connect any non-public ramp, roadway or drive to or with a public road or street in this county without first complying with the foregoing provisions of this article. Any person, corporation, or other entity desiring to build a private roadway, ramp or drive which is to join or connect with a public road in the county shall first obtain written permission from this board prior to joining or connecting the non-public roadway or drive to a public road. 
(Ord. of 6-12-1984, §§ 3, 11) 
Sec. 28-83. - Application. 
Any person, corporation or entity desiring to join or connect a non-public roadway, ramp or drive to or with a public road in the county shall first apply in writing to this board on a form, as prescribed from time to time by this board, setting forth the following information and any other information that may be required by this board from time to time: 
(1)  Name, street, mailing address and home and business telephone numbers; 
(2)  Name or location of public road or street with which applicant desires to join or connect; 
(3)  Description of non-public roadway, ramp or drive applicant desires to build, including construction materials, length, width and drainage measures; 
(4)  The type, size and total length of pipe to be used in the ramp. 
(Ord. of 6-12-1984, § 4) 
Sec. 28-84. - Construction standards and specifications. 
Each non-public roadway, drive and ramp in this county must be constructed in a workmanship-like manner, taking into consideration the terrain, soil type and anticipated usage. In addition, each non-public roadway, drive and ramp must meet as a minimum the following specifications and requirements: 
(1)  All road and street rights-of-way conveyed to the county must have an overall minimum width of 80 feet, with a graded roadbed of not less than 30 feet in the center. In addition, the outside edges of the graded road must be graded, ditched and sloped appropriately to accommodate all normal water runoff from the graded roadbed. 
(2)  All ramps constructed to join or connect a non-public driveway with a public or non-public roadway must be at least 20 feet wide if the non-public roadway or drive is a private driveway for a private single-family residence, and 30 feet wide if the non-public roadway is for any other purpose other than a driveway for a private single-family residence. 
(3)  The roadway, drive or ramp must be constructed of materials normally suitable for the type of roadway, driveway or ramp being constructed and must comply or meet with the standards of the current edition of the current edition of the state department of transportation standard specifications or such other standards which this board may adopt from time to time without the necessity of amending this article. 
(4)  Ditches, pipe and other water drainage and run-off measures will be provided and installed by applicant for each such roadway, ramp and drive as required to adequately drain and protect such roadway, ramp, or drive as well as the adjoining public and private roadways which will be affected by the water runoff from such non-public roadway, ramp, or drive. The final resolution of such drainage measures must also provide for the protection from any potential runoff damage to any then proposed streets or roadways that may be subsequently affected by the water runoff from such non-public roadway, ramp or drive. 
(5)  Construction of the roadway, driveway or ramp shall not interfere with, impede, or create a hazard to existing drainage or traffic. 
(6)  All work will be required to be performed in such a manner as not to present the county with an inferior or substandard roadway which would result in additional expenditures or undue future maintenance by the county. 
(7)  Paving is not mandatory. However if a paving is to be done, the roadway, drive or ramp must comply with all requirements of the state department of transportation standard specifications relating to paved county roads. 
(8)  Upon request of an applicant and if the board of commissioners determines it to be in the best interests of the public, the county may construct a ramp from a public right-of-way to the edge of applicant's private property, providing applicant pays in advance the cost of the pipe to be used. The county will not construct ramps from on or across non-public property or from non-public roadways. 
(9)  All pipe and other materials used by a landowner or applicant in the construction of a ramp, drive or roadway which is on, or subsequently becomes a part of, a public right-of-way become the property of the county and may not be removed by the applicant or landowner, regardless of whether the pipe or other materials were furnished by the landowner or the county. 
(10)  The location of the point of connection or joining with a public road must be first approved by the board of commissioners of the county or its authorized representative. 
(Ord. of 6-12-1984, § 5; Ord. of 2001, § 1) 
Sec. 28-85. - Requirements for acceptance of private ramp, drive or roadway by county. 
(a)  Once the non-public ramp, drive or roadway has been completed by the applicant and accepted by this board, then the applicant or owner may convey the ramp, drive or road to the county. The county shall refuse to accept such ramp, drive or roadway if it does not comply with the requirements of this article. The landowner, applicant or contractor should consult with the county board of commissioners or its authorized representative as needed during the construction of any roadway, drive or ramp if there is any question regarding compliance with this article. 
(b)  All non-public ramps, drives and roadways must be inspected by the road superintendent or some other official designated by this board prior to final approval. Approval will not be unreasonably withheld. 
(c)  Any ramp, drive or roadway conveyed to the county pursuant to this article must be free of all liens and encumbrances at the time of conveyance to the county, and proof of such must be furnished to the county prior to its acceptance of such ramp, drive or roadway. 
(Ord. of 6-12-1984, §§ 6—10) 
Sec. 28-86. - County will not aid in construction or maintain private ramps, roads or drives. 
The county shall neither furnish free of charge nor sell, lease, or rent any county property, including dirt, pipe, labor, equipment or machinery, for the construction, repair, maintenance or improvement of roadways, ramps, or driveways on or across non-public property. The county shall not cut, grade, build, or improve any roadways, ramps or driveways across non-public property. 
(Ord. of 6-12-1984, §§ 2, 3) 
Secs. 28-87—28-99. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - TIMBER OPERATIONS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note— The Timber Operations Ordinance of November 17, 2012 did not specifically amend the code, and has been included at the editor's discretion as §§ 28-100—28-110. 

Sec. 28-100. - Purpose and intent. 
This article is intended to require notice of timber harvesting operations within the unincorporated areas of Jeff Davis County pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 12-6-24, and, in accordance with Title 32 of the Official Code of Georgia, provide regulations further governing use of public roads by persons engaged in said timber harvesting operations in order to assure the public safety and to protect the county roadways and environment. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 28-101. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
County administrator means the county administrator for Jeff Davis County, or his or her designee. 
Notice means the notice required to be given to the public works department by the timber harvester as provided herein. 
Person means any natural person, firm, corporation, limited liability company, partnership, or other legal entity of whatever form. 
Road department means the Jeff Davis County Road Department. 
Road department superintendent means the superintendent of the Jeff Davis County Road Department. 
Surety bond means a valid surety bond, executed by a surety corporation authorized to transact business in the State of Georgia, protecting the county against any damage caused by such person or firm in an amount specified by the governing authority of Jeff Davis County not exceeding $5,000.00 or, at the option of the timber harvester, a valid irrevocable letter of credit issued by a bank or savings and loan association, as defined in O.C.G.A. § 7-1-4, in the amount of an in lieu of such bond. Any such surety bond or letter of credit shall be in form prescribed by or acceptable to the county administrator and shall be for the calendar year in which delivered. 
Timber means softwood or hardwood trees harvested for commercial purposes. 
Timber harvester means any person harvesting standing timber in any unincorporated area of Jeff Davis County, Georgia, for delivery as pulpwood, logs, poles, posts, or wood chips to any wood yard or processing plant located inside or outside the State of Georgia. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 28-102. - Notice required. 
Prior written notice shall be required of any timber harvester harvesting timber in the unincorporated areas of the county for each separate tract to be harvested. Said written notice shall be delivered to the road department in such form and containing such information as set forth in O.C.G.A. § 12-6-24(b)(1). Notice shall be effective only as to the tract described therein upon receipt by the road department as confirmed by written acknowledgment from said road department to the timber harvester and compliance with all other applicable requirements of this article. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 28-103. - Surety bond. 
(a)  A surety bond shall not be required prior to notice becoming effective. However, following the giving of any notice, in the event that the road department superintendent determines that any activities relating to the timber harvesting are being conducted in a manner that poses likelihood of damage to any public rights-of-way or danger to the public safety, the road department shall be authorized to demand a surety bond from the timber harvester. The surety bond shall be delivered to the road department within three business days following receipt of written demand for the same, unless within said time a written notice of appeal is received by the road department contesting the requirement of the surety bond. In the event of such contest, the road department shall, no later than five business days, schedule an administrative hearing in such matter before the county administrator, who shall deliver a decision within three business days of said hearing. The decision of the county administrator shall be conclusive and binding for all purposes. 
Following any contest as provided above, all timber harvesting authorized pursuant to the applicable notice shall be suspended until the surety bond, if any, is delivered to the road department as required by the county administrator. 
(b)  The amount of the bond shall not exceed $5,000.00. The bond shall indemnify the county against any and all damage caused, as a result of the timber harvesting and related activities, to any county roads, rights-of-way, points of egress or other public property. The surety bond shall also indemnify the county for any costs incurred in the cleanup of waste or debris left on public property as a result of the timber harvesting. 
(c)  Upon completion of any necessary repairs to public property and removal of all waste and debris, the county will release the timber harvester from the surety bond. 
(d)  In no event shall the delivery of a surety bond limit the liability of any person engaged in timber harvesting and related activities for damages to public property or rights-of-way or for other personal injury or property damage. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 28-104. - Culverts. 
Prior to commencing timber harvesting operations, the road department superintendent shall inspect the point of access to the public road from the tract described in the notice in order to determine its suitability. If a culvert is required at the point of access, it shall be promptly installed by the timber harvester as directed by the road department superintendent. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 28-105. - Signs. 
Prior to commencing any timber harvesting operations, the timber harvester shall post two signs in each direction from the point of access onto the involved public road. One sign at a distance of 1,000 feet from the point of access stating "Warning: Logging Operations Ahead," and one sign at a distance of 500 feet stating "Slow Truck Entering Highway." All signs shall be 36 inches by 36 inches, erected in a diamond shape, painted orange with black legend and posted at least three feet from the travel surface of the roadway. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 28-106. - Roadway safety. 
During the period of operations, the timber harvester shall comply with the following: 
(1)  All harvesting operations shall be conducted on the tract identified in the notice and off public roads and rights-of-way. Logging and skidding of logs on public roads and rights-of-way are strictly prohibited. 
(2)  Ditches constituting a part of the public drainage system or otherwise benefitting a public right-of-way shall be kept clear of all debris and residue at all times to permit proper drainage. 
(3)  There shall be no blockage of public roads or rights-of-way at the access site, and all public roads and rights-of-way must remain open and kept free of debris and residue at all times. 
(4)  No equipment, trucks, trailers, or other personal property shall be parked or located on any public road or right-of-way. 
(5)  Mud shall not be carried onto paved public roads by logging vehicles. Where necessary, a temporary construction exit of gravel shall be maintained by the timber harvester to eliminate any hazard to traffic or unsightly conditions on the public right-of -way. 
(6)  During periods of rain or inclement weather, logging vehicles shall not be operated over the unimproved public roads when such travel causes sufficient damage to the road system that the passage of smaller and lighter vehicles is hampered. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 28-107. - Enforcement. 
(a)  Upon notice from the issuing authority, work on any project that is being done contrary to the provisions of this article shall be immediately stopped. Such notice shall be in writing and shall be given to the timber harvester and the owner of the subject property, and shall state the conditions under which work may resume. When an emergency exists, written notice shall not be required. 
(b)  If the conditions are not brought into compliance within five business days of the notice, the road department shall be authorized to accomplish the work with costs thereof to be reimbursed by the timber harvester, and any violation of the provisions of this article shall be punished as for a misdemeanor. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 28-108. - Concluding operations. 
(a)  The timber harvester shall give written notification to the road department supervisor upon completion of the timber harvesting operations. The road department supervisor shall inspect all affected public property and public rights-of-way to assure that the same has not been damaged or has been restored to its original condition, including any shaping of ditches, grading or seeding as required. The timber harvester shall be notified in writing of any deficiencies and given 15 business days to correct said deficiencies. If not accomplished during that period, the road department or its designee shall be authorized to complete the work at the cost of the timber harvester. 
(b)  When the road department superintendent determines that the road and access site are in a proper state of repair, the superintendent shall provide a written release of liability to the timber harvester. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 28-109. - Prosecution of violations. 
(a)  Any person violating any of the provisions of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor prosecutable in the Magistrate Court of Jeff Davis County and punishable by a fine not to exceed $500.00 and imprisonment in the county jail for a period of no longer than 12 months. 
(b)  The imposition of any fine or other sentence pursuant to this section shall in no way limit the liability of any person for damage done to public property or public rights-of-way, and the county shall be authorized to additionally pursue recovery for any such damage by any and all means permitted by law or in equity, to include, without limitation, the filing of a suit for damages, or the seeking of injunctive relief to stop any such damage. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Sec. 28-110. - Timber harvesting notice. 
(a)  Prior to initiating any timber harvesting activities in the county on or after the effective date of the ordinance from which this section derives, the timber harvesting contractor shall give written notification to the board of assessors of the county within 24 hours prior to commencing start-up activities moving in of equipment or cutting of any trees. The notice shall be in the following form: 

Upon completion of the harvesting of the timber identified in the above form, the timber harvesting contractor shall give oral notification in person or by telephone to the tax assessor's office that the harvesting activities at the above described location have been completed. 
(b)  The penalty for failure to comply with the reporting requirements set out in subsection (a) of this section shall be a fine not to exceed $1,000.00 and/or 12 months imprisonment in the county jail. 
(c)  Citations for violation of this section shall be prosecuted in the Magistrate Court of Jeff Davis County. 
(Ord. of 11-17-2012) 
Chapter 30 - SOLID WASTE[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Solid waste management generally, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-20 et seq.; Georgia Comprehensive Solid Waste Management Act, O.C.G.A. § 12-9-1; hazardous waste management, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-79; local and regional solid waste plans, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-31.1; tire disposal restrictions, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-40.1; yard trimmings and disposal restrictions, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-40.2; authorization for local government units to enforce collection of taxes, fees, or assessments for solid waste management, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-39.3; authority of local governments to adopt and enforce local regulations for the handling and disposal of solid waste, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-30.9; Litter Control Law, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-40; transporting garbage or waste across state or county boundaries pursuant to contract, O.C.G.A. § 36-1-16; Resource Recovery Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-63-1 et seq.; littering highways, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-249. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 30-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Acceptable waste means waste generated from day to day living in a household. The term "acceptable waste" does not include, furniture, carpets, appliances, white goods, motor vehicle parts, sheetrock, roofing shingles, window frames, mattresses, fluorescent light tubes, building materials, and commercial waste, inert waste, which are all considered nonacceptable waste as defined by this chapter. 
City means the City of Hazelhurst, Georgia. 
Garbage means putrescible animal and vegetable wastes resulting from the handling, preparation, cooking, and consumption of food. 
Hazardous waste means: 
(1)  Solid or liquid waste material resulting from the manufacture or use of pesticides and drugs (other than normal household use); 
(2)  Pathological wastes; 
(3)  Fluorescent light tubes; 
(4)  Highly flammable or explosive wastes; 
(5)  Toxic wastes; 
(6)  Sewage sludge, asbestos, oil or petroleum by-products; and 
(7)  Other waste material determined to be a likely hazard to the public health, safety, or environment, as provided for by the laws of state or as provided for in the rules and regulations of the department of human resources, environmental protection division. 
Inert waste means vegetation, tree limbs and stumps, grass clippings, plants and shrubs. 
Putrescible wastes means wastes that are capable of being decomposed by microorganisms, including kitchen wastes, manure, offal, hatchery and poultry wastes, and garbage. 
Refuse means all putrescible and nonputrescible solid waste (except body waste) including garbage, rubbish, ashes, street cleanings, dead animals, abandoned automobiles, and solid commercial and industrial wastes. 
Rubbish means nonputrescible solid waste (excluding ashes), consisting of both combustible and noncombustible waste, such as paper, cardboard, tin cans, wood, glass, bedding, crockery, and similar materials. 
Solid waste means putrescible and nonputrescible wastes, except water, carried body wastes, including garbage, rubbish, ashes, street refuse, dead animals, sewage sludge, animal manures, industrial wastes, residue from incineration, food processing wastes, construction waste, hazardous waste, and any other waste material in a solid or semisolid state not otherwise defined in this article. 
State law specifically includes the Georgia Comprehensive Solid Waste Management Act, O.C.G.A. § 12-9-1 et seq. 
Transfer station means the Jeff Davis County-City of Hazlehurst Solid Waste Transfer Station. 
(Ord. of 10-13-2005, § 2) 
Sec. 30-2. - Penalties for violation. 
Except as otherwise specifically provided in this chapter, any person proven of violating the terms of this chapter shall be fined up to a maximum of $500.00 for the first offense, $750.00 for the second offense, and $1,000.00 for the third offense, or confined to 30 days in the public jail of this county for each violation, with the violator to pay the costs of prosecution. 
(Ord. of 10-13-2005, § 8) 
Sec. 30-3. - Dumping and unauthorized disposal prohibited. 
No person shall dump, dispose of, discard, or throw away any garbage, hazardous waste, putrescible or nonputrescible waste, refuse, solid waste, building material, commercial waste, or other rubbish, upon any road right-of-way, parkway, ditch, pond, watercourse, stream, river, or any other public place, or the lands of another, excepting only county authorized and maintained public dump sites, and waste disposal receptacles, with the exception of hazardous waste, which will not be accepted at any solid waste facility in the county. It shall be an offense to dump, dispose of, discard any waste materials not designated as acceptable at any county authorized and maintained public dump site, other than a site nominated for such waste. 
(Ord. of 10-13-2005, § 3) 
Sec. 30-4. - Creating public nuisance by disposal of waste prohibited. 
No person or other entity shall dispose of any waste, garbage, refuse, or rubbish, in such a manner as to create a public nuisance or public health hazard, contravening the terms as defined by state law. 
(Ord. of 10-13-2005, § 4) 
Sec. 30-5. - Scavenging or otherwise tampering with waste prohibited. 
No person shall scavenge, remove, disturb any item whatsoever from any county designated waste disposal site, or waste receptacle therein. 
(Ord. of 10-13-2005, § 5) 
Sec. 30-6. - County public dump site to be used only by county residents. 
Any county authorized and maintained public dump site shall be for the use of county residents exclusively. 
(Ord. of 10-13-2005, § 6) 
Sec. 30-7. - Name on unlawfully disposed items creates presumption of guilt. 
Any refuse, or other type of waste as defined in this article that is dumped, deposited, thrown, or left upon any road right-of-way, parkway, ditch, pond, watercourse, stream, river, or any other public place, or the lands of others, in violation of this chapter is discovered to contain any article or articles, including, but not limited to letters, bills, publications, or other writings that display the name of a person thereon in such a manner as to indicate that the article belongs or belonged to such person, it shall be a presumption that such person has violated this article, unless proven otherwise by the alleged violator. 
(Ord. of 10-13-2005, § 7) 
Sec. 30-8. - Authority of county and state law enforcement officers and courts to enforce. 
County and state law enforcement officers are authorized to enforce the provisions of this chapter and the courts of the county and state are authorized to try individuals accused of violating this article and, upon conviction, to assess the penalties provided for herein. 
(Ord. of 10-13-2005, § 9) 
Secs. 30-9—30-34. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - TRANSFER STATION 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 30-35. - All solid waste from county to be delivered to transfer station. 
Except as otherwise provided herein, all county solid waste generated within the unincorporated area of the county must be delivered to the transfer station for transfer to an out of county solid waste disposal site approved by the board of commissioners from time to time. All private collectors and haulers of solid waste in the unincorporated area of the county must deliver all such waste to the transfer station. 
(Ord. of 11-9-2006, §§ A, C) 
Sec. 30-36. - Disposal fees. 
All county solid waste delivered to the transfer station shall be subject to uniform fees, as approved from time to time by the board of commissioners consistent with applicable law, regardless of whether such solid waste is delivered by an authorized public or private hauler. The board of commissioners may authorize such fees to be revised from time to time with such fee changes or revisions constituting an amendment to this article. 
(Ord. of 11-9-2006, § B) 
Sec. 30-37. - Only county, city and private haulers may deposit waste at transfer station. 
(a)  The transfer station shall only be open to receive solid waste from vehicles operated by the county, the city, and private haulers who have received a permit issued by the county or the city or their authorized designees pursuant to this article. Individuals and businesses that are not in the regular business of hauling solid waste shall not be permitted to deliver any solid wastes to the transfer station. 
(b)  All persons and entities in the county needing to dispose of solid waste other than the city, the county and authorized private haulers who have obtained permits as provided in this chapter, must take their solid waste to other collection sites which have been, or will be, duly designated by the county and city to receive such solid waste. 
(Ord. of 11-9-2006, §§ G, H) 
Sec. 30-38. - Wastes accepted at transfer station; excluded wastes. 
Only solid waste as defined by federal and state laws and regulations will be accepted at the transfer station, and all solid waste shall be subject to the following exclusions: 
(1)  Waste containing any of the following will be excluded and shall not be delivered to or accepted at the transfer station: lead, batteries, fluorescent and incandescent laps or ballasts, appliances, yard waste, radioactive waste, medical waste or flammable, explosive, or any waste regulated as hazardous waste by state or federal laws and regulations; all of the foregoing shall be classified as excluded waste. 
(2)  In addition, special waste, including asbestos containing material and sewerage sludge will be accepted only after receiving approval from the private hauler which is authorized to pick up and transport waste materials from the transfer station to final disposal sites. Any persons or entities wanting to dispose of any such special waste must make arrangements directly with the private hauler servicing the transfer station. 
(Ord. of 11-9-2006, § J) 
Sec. 30-39. - Identification passes. 
The county, in coordination with the city, will develop and implement an identification pass for all vehicles authorized to bring solid waste to the transfer station, and no vehicle shall be permitted to dispose of any solid waste at the transfer station without a proper identification or pass. 
(Ord. of 11-9-2006, § I) 
Secs. 30-40—30-66. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PRIVATE WASTE HAULERS 

Sec. 30-67. - When collection permit required; term; fees. 
(a)  Any legal entity desiring to collect municipal solid waste generated within the unincorporated area of the county on a commercial basis for disposal at the transfer station must first obtain a collection permit from the county board of commissioners, or its authorized designee. The permit shall be issued for collection of solid waste and shall be separate and apart from any other licensing requirement. 
(b)  Unless sooner revoked for violation of this division, such permit shall automatically terminate at midnight on December 31 each year. 
(c)  There shall be no charge for permits issued to the city or the county or to vehicles operated by them; however, the county, in coordination with the city, may set a permit fee for private haulers to offset the administration cost of issuing the permit. Any fee schedule for such permits may be set and revised from time to time by the board of county commissioners and the city governing authority without the same constituting an amendment to this article. 
(Ord. of 11-9-2006, § D) 
Sec. 30-68. - Tipping fees to be established and approved by county and city. 
The private hauler responsible for transporting the solid waste from the transfer station will establish tipping fees at the transfer station, which fees must be approved by the county and the city. 
(Ord. of 11-9-2006, § L) 
Sec. 30-69. - Out-of-county waste may be deposited by private hauler. 
The private hauler may also accept solid waste from haulers outside of the county as long as the waste is of the same type that is otherwise permitted to be taken to the transfer station. The private hauler will set tipping fees for such haulers of out-of-county waste. Private haulers may not accept any out-of-county waste which would constitute excluded waste under this article. 
(Ord. of 11-9-2006, § M) 
Sec. 30-70. - Separation and removal of excluded materials; costs. 
Any waste materials brought to the transfer station by a private hauler that are not accepted shall be promptly separated and removed by the private hauler at the sole expense of the private hauler. Should any private hauler fail to separate and remove excluded waste or any other waste that cannot be accepted at the transfer station, the private hauler shall be liable for all costs incurred by the county or city in separating or returning such excluded waste to the private hauler or all additional costs incurred by the county or city in disposing of such excluded waste. 
(Ord. of 11-9-2006, § N) 
Sec. 30-71. - Violations and penalties. 
(a)  Any individual or legal entity required to obtain a collection permit under this division that fails to deliver solid waste for disposal at the transfer station shall be in violation of this article punishable by a civil fine in the amount of $1,000.00 per offense and revocation of the collection permit. 
(b)  Any individual or entity not required to obtain a collection permit under this article disposing of solid waste generated within the unincorporated area of the county who fails to deliver such solid waste to the transfer station there is hereby imposed a civil fine of up to a maximum of $100.00 per offense. 
(c)  Each bulk container or garbage receptacle of county solid waste generated within the unincorporated area of the county and collected but not delivered to the county transfer station for disposal shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 11-9-2006, §§ E, F) 
Chapter 32 - TAXATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Revenue and taxation generally, O.C.G.A. § 48-1-1 et seq.; ad valorem taxation of property, O.C.G.A. § 48-5-1 et seq.; county tax officials and administration, O.C.G.A. § 48-5-100 et seq.; county taxation, O.C.G.A. § 48-5-220 et seq.; municipal taxation, O.C.G.A. § 48-5-350 et seq.; miscellaneous local administration provisions, O.C.G.A. § 48-5-380; sales and use taxes, O.C.G.A. § 48-8-1 et seq.; taxes on tobacco products, O.C.G.A. § 48-11-1 et seq.; levy of occupation taxes by counties and municipalities on certain businesses, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-1 et seq.; imposition of regulatory fees by local governments on certain businesses, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-8 et seq.; authority of counties and municipalities to impose excise tax on lodging and accommodations, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-51. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 32-1. - Judicial in rem tax foreclosures authorized for collection of ad valorem taxes. 
Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-4-75 et seq., the county may undertake judicial in rem tax foreclosures for delinquent ad valorem taxes. 
(Res. of 8-15-2011(1)) 
Sec. 32-2. - Minimum number of acres for conservation use exemption; exception. 
(a)  The county establishes the minimum number of acres for qualified current use property for the county at 20 acres. No property owner may take advantage of the conservation use exemption if they own less that 20 acres, except as provided in this section. 
(b)  Property owners applying for the conservation use exemption for parcels of less than 20 acres may qualify for the exemption if they provide copies of two previous years' federal income tax returns (Schedule F, Form 1040, profit or loss statement from farming activity) showing a continuous agricultural business use for a period greater than one year. 
(Res. of 8-15-2011(2)) 
Secs. 32-3—32-22. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - LODGING AND ACCOMMODATIONS TAX[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Authority of counties and municipalities to impose excise tax on lodging and accommodations, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-51. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 32-23. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning. 
City means the City of Hazelhurst, Georgia. 
County means all of the territory within the geographic boundaries of the county, state, including all municipalities located therein. The entirety of the county shall constitute the territorial limits of the special tax district as contemplated by O.C.G.A. § 48-13-50.1. 
Due date means the 20th day after the end of the monthly period for which the tax is to be computed. 
Guest room means a room occupied, or intended, arranged or designed for occupancy by one or more occupants for the purpose of living quarters or residential use. 
Monthly period means a calendar month. 
Motel means any structure or any portion of a structure, including any motel, lodginghouse, roominghouse, dormitory, Turkish bath, bachelor hotel, hotel, motor hotel, auto court, inn, bed and breakfast inn, public club, or private club, containing guest rooms and which is occupied, or is intended or designed for occupancy by guests, whether rent is paid in money, goods, labor, or otherwise. The term "motel" does not include any convalescent center, nursing home, hospital, jail, asylum, sanitarium, orphanage, prison, detention center, or other buildings in which human beings are housed and detained under legal restraint. For purposes of this article, the term "motel" also includes the term "hotel." 
Occupancy means the use or possession, or the right to the use or possession of any room or apartment in a motel, or the right to the use or possession of the furnishing or to the services and accommodations accompanying the use and possession of the room. 
Occupant or guest means any person who, for a consideration, uses, possesses, or has the right to use or possess any room in a motel under any lease, concession, permit, right of access, license to use, or other agreement, or otherwise. 
Operator means any person operating a motel in the county, including, but not limited to, the owner or proprietor of such premises, the leasee, sublessee, lender in possession, licensee or any other person otherwise operating such motel. 
Person means an individual, firm, partnership, joint venture, association, social club, fraternal organization, joint stock company, corporation, nonprofit corporation or cooperative nonprofit membership, estate, trust, business trust, receiver, trustee, syndicate, or any other group or combination acting as a unit, the plural as well as the singular number, excepting the United States of America, the state, and any political subdivision of either thereof upon which the county is without power to impose the tax herein provided. 
Rent means the consideration received for occupancy valued in money, whether received in money or otherwise, including all receipts, cash, credits, and property or services of any kind or nature, and also the amount for which credit is allowed by the operator to the occupant, without any deduction therefrom whatsoever. 
Return means any return filed or required to be filed as provided in this article. 
Tax commissioner means the county tax commissioner. 
Tax means the tax imposed by this article. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 1) 
Sec. 32-24. - Levied. 
Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-13-50 et seq., the county levies and imposed a tax of five percent of the rent for every occupancy of a guest room in a motel in the county, including all municipalities located therein; provided, however, that no tax shall be levied as provided in this section upon the fees or charges for any rooms, lodgings, or accommodations furnished for use as meeting rooms. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 2) 
Sec. 32-25. - Collection of tax by operator. 
It shall be the duty of every operator of a motel located within the county to collect from the occupants the tax levied and imposed upon the occupancy of guest rooms by the provisions of this article. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 3) 
Sec. 32-26. - Exemptions. 
Notwithstanding any other provision of this article, no tax shall be levied as provided in this article upon the fees or charges for any rooms, lodgings or accommodations furnished for use by state or local governmental officials or employees when traveling on official business. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 4) 
Sec. 32-27. - Notification to operators. 
Within five days after learning of the opening or establishment of any new business subject to this article, the county administrator shall send a notice of the duty to collect established in this article, together with a copy article to such new business. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 5) 
Sec. 32-28. - Due date of taxes. 
All taxes levied and imposed by this article shall be due and payable to the county monthly on or before the 20th day of every month next succeeding each respective monthly period in which such taxes are collected. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 6) 
Sec. 32-29. - Returns and time of filing; remittance of tax. 
(a)  On or before the 20th day of the month following each monthly period, a return for the preceding monthly period shall be filed with the county tax commissioner in such form as the tax commissioner may prescribe by every operator liable for the payment of tax hereunder. 
(b)  All returns shall show the gross rent, exempt rent, taxable rent, amount of tax collected or otherwise due for the monthly period for which filed, and such other information as may be required by the tax commissioner and shall be accompanied when filed by remittance of the net amount of tax due. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 7) 
Sec. 32-30. - Deficiency determinations. 
(a)  Computation of tax; authority to make; basis of computation. If the tax commissioner is not satisfied with the return of the tax or the amount of the tax required to be paid to the county by any person or business subject to this article, he may compute and determine the amount required to be paid upon the basis of any information in his possession or which may come into his possession. One or more than one deficiency determinations may be made for the amount due for one or more than one monthly period. 
(b)  Interest on deficiency. The amount of the unpaid tax found to be due shall bear interest at the rate of three-fourths of one percent per month from and after the 20th day of the month following the monthly period for which the amount shall have been returned until the date of payment of such tax and interest. 
(c)  Offsetting of overpayments. In making a determination the tax commissioner may offset overpayments for a period, or periods, against unpaid tax found to be due for another period or periods, against penalties, and against the interest on such unpaid tax. 
(d)  Notice of determination. The tax commissioner, or his designated representative, shall give to the operator written notice of his determination. The notice may be served personally or by mail. If by mail, such service shall be addressed to the operator at his address as it appears in the records of the tax commissioner. 
(e)  Time within which notice of deficiency determination to be mailed. Except in the case of failure to make a return, every notice of a deficiency determination shall be mailed within three years after the 20th day of the calendar month following the monthly period for which the amount is proposed to be determined, or within three years after the return is filed, whichever period shall last expire. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 8) 
Sec. 32-31. - Determination if no return made. 
(a)  Estimate of gross receipts. If any operator fails to make a return, the tax commissioner shall make an estimate of the amount of the gross receipts of the operator in this county which are subject to the tax. The estimate shall be made for the period in respect to which the person or business failed to make the return and shall be based upon any information which is or may come into the possession of the tax commissioner. Upon the basis of this estimate the tax commissioner shall compute and determine the amount required to be paid the county adding to the sum thus determined a penalty equal to 15 percent thereof. One or more determinations may be made of the amount due for one or for more than one monthly period. 
(b)  Offsetting of overpayments. In making a determination the tax commissioner may offset overpayments for a period against unpaid tax found to be due for another period, against penalties, and against interest on unpaid tax found to be due. The interest on such unpaid tax shall be computed in the manner set forth in this section. 
(c)  Interest on amount found due. The amount of the unpaid tax found to be due shall bear interest at the rate of three-fourths of one percent per month from and after the 20th day of the month following the monthly period for which the amount should have been returned until the date of payment of such tax, penalties, and interest. 
(d)  Notice of determination. Promptly after making his determination, the tax commissioner shall give to the operator written notice of his determination, which notice may be served personally or by mail in the manner prescribed for service of notice of a deficiency determination. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 9) 
Sec. 32-32. - Collection of tax. 
(a)  When it is determined by a return filed, or by the tax commissioner having made a determination pursuant to this article that tax is due and payable to the county under the provisions of this article, the tax commissioner may at any time within three years after determination that such tax is due and payable bring an action in the courts of this state, of any other state, or of the United States in the name of the county to collect the amount of tax payable to the county together with interest thereon and penalties, court costs, attorney's fees and other legal fees incident thereto. The bringing of such an action shall not be a prerequisite for the issuance of a fi. fa. under the provisions of this section. 
(b)  If any operator liable for any amount of tax under this article sells or transfers his business, his successors or assigns shall withhold a sufficient amount of the purchase price of the business to cover such amount of tax, interest thereon, and penalties, and pay such sum over to the county unless the operator liable for such tax delivers to such purchaser or transferee as the case may be, at the time of such sale or transfer, a certificate from the tax commissioner showing that all tax returns required of such operator have been filed and all taxes shown as being payable on those returns pursuant to this article have been paid in full. 
(c)  If the purchaser or transferee of a business fails to withhold the required amount of the purchase price, he shall be personally liable for the payment of the amount required to be withheld by him to the extent of the purchase price, valued in money. The time within which the obligations of successor may be enforced shall start to run at the time the operator sells or transfers his business, or at the time that the determination against the operator becomes final, whichever event occurs later. 
(d)  The tax commissioner is hereby authorized to issue a fi. fa. for execution and levy to satisfy the amount of any tax, penalty or interest due but not paid under the provisions of this article. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 10) 
Sec. 32-33. - Administration. 
(a)  The tax commissioner shall administer and enforce the provision of this article for the levy and collection of the tax imposed by this article, and shall remit all such taxes collected to the Hazlehurst-the county board of tourism (hereinafter sometimes referred to as the board of tourism) no later than the 20th day of the month following the month of collection. There shall be no charge to the board of tourism for this service. 
(b)  All funds so collected and disbursed to the board of tourism shall be held by the board of tourism in trust for the citizens of the county and may only be spent and disbursed in accordance with this article and any contract entered into between the board of commissioners and the board of tourism. 
(c)  The county administrator shall have the power and authority to make and publish reasonable rules and regulations not inconsistent with this article or other ordinances of the county, state law, or the state or federal constitutions, for the administration and enforcement of the provisions of this article and the collection of the taxes hereunder. 
(d)  Every operator shall keep such records, receipts, invoices, and other pertinent papers in such form as the county administrator or tax commissioner may require. 
(e)  The tax commissioner or county administrator, or any person authorized in writing by either of them, may examine the books, papers, records, financial reports, equipment and other facilities of any operator in order to verify the accuracy of any return made, or if no return is made by the operator, to ascertain and determine the amount of tax required to be paid. 
(f)  In the administration of the provisions of this article, the county administrator or tax commissioner may require the filing of the reports by any person or class of persons having in such person's or persons' possession or custody information relating to rentals of guestrooms which are subject to the tax. The reports shall be filed with the official requesting such reports when required by the county administrator or tax commissioner and shall set forth the rental charged for each occupancy, the date or dates of occupancy, and such other information as the requesting official may require. 
(g)  Any information or records requested by or furnished to the county administrator or tax commissioner pursuant to a request under this article, and not specifically used for tax liability calculations, or the review of the operator's calculations and not placed in the records of the county or tax commissioner, shall be considered confidential. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 11) 
Sec. 32-34. - Agents for receiving notices. 
Each operator shall notify the county administrator, in writing, of the name of an agent to receive for the operator any notice required to be given to the operator under the provisions of this article, stating the full name, street address, mailing address and telephone number of such agent. The operator shall also notify the county administrator in writing each time a replacement agent is appointed. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 12) 
Sec. 32-35. - Use of taxes. 
All monies collected from the levy of the tax imposed hereby shall be expressly and exclusively used to enhance and expand the economies of the city and the county through the promotion of tourism. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 14) 
Sec. 32-36. - Penalty. 
(a)  Violation of this article shall be punishable as a misdemeanor and each person shall be guilty of a separate offense for each and every day or portion thereof during which any violation of any provision of this article is committed, continued, or permitted by such person, and shall be punished accordingly. 
(b)  Any operator or other person who fails to register as required herein, or to furnish any return required to be made, or who fails or refuses to furnish a supplemental return or other data required by the county administrator or tax commissioner or who renders a false or fraudulent return shall be deemed guilty of an offense and upon conviction thereof shall be punished as provided in this section. 
(c)  Any person required to make, render, sign, or verify any report who makes any false or fraudulent report, with intent to defeat or evade the determination of an amount due required by this article to be made shall be deemed guilty of an offense and upon conviction thereof shall be punished as provided in this section. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 13) 
Secs. 32-37—32-60. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - BOARD OF TOURISM 

Sec. 32-61. - Joint city-county board of tourism. 
(a)  The county has created and established a board of tourism which shall be known as the Hazlehurst-Jeff Davis County Board of Tourism. The board of tourism shall be the official body for the promotion of tourism in the city and the county. 
(b)  All taxes collected by the tax commissioner pursuant to this article shall be remitted to the board of tourism to be used as provided herein. The board of tourism shall use the tax monies collected and remitted to it pursuant to this article solely for purposes of enhancing and expanding the economies of the city and the county through the promotion of tourism. 
(c)  The county shall enter into a contract with the board of tourism regarding the authority of the board, the transfer of such tax funds to the board, the use of the funds, and the accountability of the board for such funds. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 15) 
Sec. 32-62. - Purpose; composition and appointment. 
(a)  The purpose of the board of tourism is to plan, coordinate, and administer an effective tourism program for the county, pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-13-50 et seq. 
(b)  The board of tourism shall consist of nine members. Members of the board shall be appointed from the following areas for the following initial terms: 

 
(c)  Persons representing the governmental bodies may, but are not required to be, elected members of the bodies. The city mayor, the chairperson of the county board of commissioners and the president of the chamber of commerce shall be ex-officio members of the board. 
(d)  Members of the board shall be appointed for staggered terms of six years, following the expiration of the initial appointed terms of the members of the board of tourism, or until their successors have been appointed and take office. Members of the board of tourism may succeed themselves and be reappointed without limitation. 
(e)  The executive director of the chamber of commerce shall serve as the chief executive officer of the board, and shall perform all financial, secretarial and other ministerial functions of the board. The chairperson of the board of tourism shall be chosen from the membership of the board. 
(f)  The board of tourism shall operate in compliance with by-laws adopted by the board. 
(g)  The city will appoint one member to represent the city, and the board of commissioners of the county will appoint one member to represent the county board of commissioners. All remaining members shall be selected and appointed as follows: 
(1)  The chamber of commerce shall submit to the county board of commissioners' nominations for a representative from each of the other seven areas of interest. 
(2)  The chamber may permit each of the other organizations or areas of interest to make a recommendation to the chamber, but all nominations made to the board of commissioners for the other seven areas of interest must come directly from the chamber of commerce. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 16) 
Sec. 32-63. - Reports and audit of board of tourism. 
The executive director of the board of tourism shall publish the minutes of all meetings; maintain a full accounting of all funds; publish, not less than quarterly, a report of activities and financial statement to the city council and the county board of commissioners. The members of the board of tourism shall also cause an annual audit of the funds of the board by a certified public accountant licensed to perform the services in the state and provide a copy of same to the city council and the county board of commissioners. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 17) 
Sec. 32-64. - Salaries and expenses of the board of tourism. 
The appointed members of the board of tourism shall serve without pay. However, the members shall be reimbursed for their reasonable expenses incurred on behalf of the board. The board of tourism is authorized to pay all of its reasonable operating expenses from the tax funds collected and remitted to it hereunder, including reasonable rent, utilities and a portion of the salary of the executive director of the chamber of commerce commiserate with his services to the board. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 18) 
Sec. 32-65. - Termination or dissolution of board of tourism. 
In the event the board of tourism should terminate, be abolished or otherwise cease to exist, all funds remaining in the hands of the board of tourism shall immediately revert and be returned to the board of commissioners, and the board of tourism shall in such event also prepare and submit a final report and audit. 
(Ord. of 9-29-1994, § 19)
